%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{One-Defect Acceptance Reduction and the \texorpdfstring{$\mu_\infty$}{mu∞}-First Audit}

\subsection{General one-defect criterion}

Assume the one-defect/one-mode reduction has already produced the effective radial-core coefficients
\begin{equation}
a_0=\frac{\xi_E g_E+\xi_c g_c}{z_{0,0}},
\qquad
b_0=\frac{\xi_E g_E}{z_{0,0}},
\qquad
c_0=\frac{\xi_O g_O}{z_{0,0}},
\label{eq:a0b0c0_general}
\end{equation}
together with the bulk mass parameter
\begin{equation}
\mu_\infty
=
\frac{m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)}{z_0(\sigma_\infty)}.
\label{eq:muinf_def}
\end{equation}

For the projected lowest channel \(\kappa_*\), a practical sufficient one-mode criterion is
\begin{equation}
\mu_\infty>0,
\qquad
a_0>0,
\qquad
b_0>0,
\qquad
\frac{|\kappa_*|\,b_0}{a_0}>\frac12,
\label{eq:practical_general_criterion}
\end{equation}
supplemented by competitor exclusion and remote-gap control.

\subsection{Lowest-channel reduction}

We now specialize to the practically most relevant lowest-channel case
\begin{equation}
|\kappa_*|=1.
\label{eq:kappastar_one}
\end{equation}
Then \eqref{eq:practical_general_criterion} becomes
\begin{equation}
\mu_\infty>0,
\qquad
a_0>0,
\qquad
b_0>0,
\qquad
2b_0>a_0.
\label{eq:criterion_kappa1}
\end{equation}

Introduce the dimensionless longitudinal burden ratio
\begin{equation}
R_c:=\frac{\xi_c g_c}{\xi_E g_E},
\label{eq:Rc_def}
\end{equation}
whenever \(\xi_E g_E\neq 0\). Then
\begin{equation}
a_0
=
\frac{\xi_E g_E}{z_{0,0}}(1+R_c)
=
b_0(1+R_c).
\label{eq:a0_equals_b0}
\end{equation}

Hence the conditions in \eqref{eq:criterion_kappa1} can be rewritten algebraically.

\begin{theorem}[Lowest-channel acceptance window]
Assume
\begin{equation}
z_{0,0}>0,
\qquad
\xi_E>0,
\qquad
|\kappa_*|=1.
\label{eq:lowest_assumptions}
\end{equation}
Then the inequalities
\begin{equation}
a_0>0,
\qquad
b_0>0,
\qquad
2b_0>a_0
\label{eq:abc_window_start}
\end{equation}
are equivalent to
\begin{equation}
\xi_E g_E>0,
\qquad
-1<R_c<1.
\label{eq:Rc_window}
\end{equation}
Therefore the one-defect acceptance criterion reduces to
\begin{equation}
\mu_\infty>0,
\qquad
\xi_E g_E>0,
\qquad
-1<R_c<1,
\label{eq:criterion_Rc_form}
\end{equation}
plus competitor exclusion and remote-gap control.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Since \(z_{0,0}>0\), one has
\[
b_0>0
\iff
\xi_E g_E>0.
\]
Using \eqref{eq:a0_equals_b0}, the inequality \(a_0>0\) becomes
\[
b_0(1+R_c)>0.
\]
Because \(b_0>0\), this is equivalent to
\[
1+R_c>0.
\]
Likewise,
\[
2b_0>a_0=b_0(1+R_c)
\]
is equivalent, after dividing by \(b_0>0\), to
\[
2>1+R_c
\iff
R_c<1.
\]
Combining with \(1+R_c>0\) gives
\[
-1<R_c<1.
\]
This proves the equivalence.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Equivalent sharp form in the transport variables}

The inequality \(2b_0>a_0\) is exactly
\begin{equation}
2\,\xi_E g_E>\xi_E g_E+\xi_c g_c
\iff
\xi_E g_E>\xi_c g_c.
\label{eq:sharp_transport_form}
\end{equation}
Hence in the lowest-channel case one may equivalently write
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty>0,
\qquad
\xi_E g_E>0,
\qquad
\xi_E g_E>\xi_c g_c.
}
\label{eq:lowest_transport_sharp}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Specialization to the explicit canonical branch}

Now specialize further to the explicit canonical branch
\begin{equation}
T_\star=T^1,
\qquad
\gamma_E=1,
\qquad
\gamma_O=0.
\label{eq:explicit_branch}
\end{equation}
On this branch one has
\begin{equation}
g_O=0,
\label{eq:gO_zero}
\end{equation}
so the odd channel drops out of the acceptance count.

Define \(R_c\) by
\begin{equation}
R_c=\frac{\xi_c g_c}{\xi_E g_E}.
\label{eq:Rc_branch_def}
\end{equation}
If the explicit branch formulas yield
\begin{equation}
R_c
=
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\,
\frac{3}{32}\,
\alpha_X(\theta_0\kappa)^2,
\label{eq:Rc_explicit}
\end{equation}
then the window \(-1<R_c<1\) becomes
\begin{equation}
\left|
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}
\right|
<
\frac{32}{3|\alpha_X|(\theta_0\kappa)^2}.
\label{eq:Rc_explicit_window}
\end{equation}

Similarly, if the branch-level even coefficient satisfies
\begin{equation}
g_E=\alpha
\propto
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,\theta_0\kappa,
\label{eq:gE_branch_sign}
\end{equation}
then the positivity condition \(\xi_E g_E>0\) reduces, for \(\xi_E>0\), to
\begin{equation}
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,\theta_0\kappa>0.
\label{eq:alpha_positive_branch}
\end{equation}

Therefore the explicit branch acceptance conditions become
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}
\right|
<
\frac{32}{3|\alpha_X|(\theta_0\kappa)^2},
\qquad
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,\theta_0\kappa>0,
\qquad
\mu_\infty>0,
}
\label{eq:explicit_branch_acceptance_pre}
\end{equation}
plus remote-gap control.

\subsection{The \texorpdfstring{$\mu_\infty$}{mu∞} sign audit}

The bulk mass sign is controlled by
\begin{equation}
\mu_\infty
=
\frac{m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)}{z_0(\sigma_\infty)}.
\label{eq:muinf_repeat}
\end{equation}
Assume
\begin{equation}
z_0(\sigma_\infty)>0.
\label{eq:z0_positive}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{sgn}\mu_\infty
=
\operatorname{sgn}\!\Bigl(m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)\Bigr).
\label{eq:muinf_sign}
\end{equation}

This yields the following practical cases.

\paragraph{Case A: \(u_X(\sigma_\infty)\ge 0\), \(\chi_\infty\ge 0\).}
Then the Class-II asymptotic correction lowers the gap, so one needs
\begin{equation}
m(\sigma_\infty)>3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)\ge 0.
\label{eq:mu_caseA_latex}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Case B: \(u_X(\sigma_\infty)\le 0\), \(\chi_\infty\ge 0\).}
Then the Class-II asymptotic correction helps the gap, so it is enough that
\begin{equation}
m(\sigma_\infty)>3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty),
\label{eq:mu_caseB_latex}
\end{equation}
which is weaker than demanding \(m(\sigma_\infty)>0\).

\paragraph{Case C: sign-indefinite asymptotic sector.}
Then one must perform the exact finite sign audit
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{sgn}\mu_\infty
=
\operatorname{sgn}\!\Bigl(m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)\Bigr).
\label{eq:mu_caseC_latex}
\end{equation}

\begin{proposition}[Earliest kill condition]
If
\begin{equation}
m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)\le 0
\qquad
\text{and}
\qquad
z_0(\sigma_\infty)>0,
\label{eq:kill_condition}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\mu_\infty\le 0,
\end{equation}
so the branch is rejected before any \(g_E\), \(g_c\), or channel-comparison insertion.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Immediate from \eqref{eq:muinf_repeat}.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Final practical theorem for the explicit branch}

\begin{theorem}[Practical explicit-branch one-defect acceptance]
Assume:
\begin{enumerate}
\item \(z_0(\sigma_\infty)>0\);
\item the lowest projected channel satisfies \(|\kappa_*|=1\);
\item the branch is the explicit canonical branch \eqref{eq:explicit_branch};
\item the remote-gap condition holds:
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
\label{eq:remote_gap_final}
\end{equation}
\end{enumerate}
Then a sufficient practical one-defect acceptance criterion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}
\right|
<
\frac{32}{3|\alpha_X|(\theta_0\kappa)^2},
\qquad
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,\theta_0\kappa>0,
\qquad
m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)>0,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:final_four_scalar_checks}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, in the more invariant transport notation,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-1<R_c<1,
\qquad
\alpha>0,
\qquad
\mu_\infty>0,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:final_four_scalar_checks_invariant}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Combine:
\begin{itemize}
\item the lowest-channel equivalence theorem \eqref{eq:criterion_Rc_form},
\item the explicit branch specialization \eqref{eq:Rc_explicit_window} and \eqref{eq:alpha_positive_branch},
\item the bulk sign reduction \eqref{eq:muinf_sign},
\item and the independent support condition \eqref{eq:remote_gap_final}.
\end{itemize}
This yields \eqref{eq:final_four_scalar_checks}, hence also \eqref{eq:final_four_scalar_checks_invariant}.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Honest status}

The symbolic reduction is now complete:
the explicit branch has been reduced to four finite scalar checks.

What is not yet inserted is the actual asymptotic branch data
\[
m(\sigma_\infty),
\qquad
u_X(\sigma_\infty),
\qquad
\chi_\infty,
\qquad
z_0(\sigma_\infty),
\]
together with the actual branch values of
\[
\xi_c,\qquad \xi_E,\qquad \Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}-\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
\]
So the next frontier is explicit evaluation, not further structural reduction.

\section{Final Summary}

The C4 one-defect acceptance problem is no longer a broad conceptual question.
In the lowest-channel case \(|\kappa_*|=1\), it reduces to
\[
\mu_\infty>0,
\qquad
\xi_E g_E>0,
\qquad
\xi_E g_E>\xi_c g_c,
\]
equivalently
\[
-1<R_c<1,
\qquad
R_c:=\frac{\xi_c g_c}{\xi_E g_E},
\]
together with remote-gap control.

For the explicit canonical branch
\[
T_\star=T^1,
\qquad
\gamma_E=1,
\qquad
\gamma_O=0,
\]
this becomes the four-scalar practical test
\[
\boxed{
\left|
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}
\right|
<
\frac{32}{3|\alpha_X|(\theta_0\kappa)^2},
\qquad
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,\theta_0\kappa>0,
\qquad
m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)>0,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\]

Thus the remaining frontier is not structural.
It is the explicit branch evaluation of
\[
m(\sigma_\infty),\quad
u_X(\sigma_\infty),\quad
\chi_\infty,\quad
z_0(\sigma_\infty),\quad
\xi_c,\quad
\xi_E,
\quad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}-\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{The \texorpdfstring{$\mu_\infty$}{mu∞}-First Audit as a Complete Finite Scalar Reduction}

\section{Goal}

At the current C4 / one-defect acceptance stage, the correct first task is to decide the sign of
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty
=
\frac{m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)}{z_0(\sigma_\infty)}.
}
\label{eq:muinf_goal}
\end{equation}
This is the earliest kill condition in the full one-defect audit.

The purpose of this section is to show that the bulk sign problem is no longer conceptual:
it is completely reduced to a finite asymptotic scalar audit.

\section{1. Bulk mass parameter from the locked Class II defect background}

In the locked Class II background, the mediator-corrected defect mass is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_{\rm eff}(x)
=
m(\bar\sigma(x)) - 3\chi_X(x)\,u_X(\bar\sigma(x)).
}
\label{eq:meff_x}
\end{equation}
The asymptotic one-defect bulk mass parameter is therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty
=
\frac{m_{\rm eff}(\infty)}{z_0(\sigma_\infty)}
=
\frac{m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)}{z_0(\sigma_\infty)}.
}
\label{eq:muinf_from_meff}
\end{equation}

Thus the bulk acceptance problem depends only on the four asymptotic scalars
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m(\sigma_\infty),\qquad
u_X(\sigma_\infty),\qquad
\chi_\infty,\qquad
z_0(\sigma_\infty).
}
\label{eq:four_bulk_scalars}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Sign reduction theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Exact sign reduction for \(\mu_\infty\)]
Assume
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
z_0(\sigma_\infty)>0.
}
\label{eq:z0_positive_assump}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{sgn}\mu_\infty
=
\operatorname{sgn}\!\Bigl(m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:mu_sign_reduction}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty>0
\iff
m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)>0.
}
\label{eq:mu_positive_equiv}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
This is immediate from \eqref{eq:muinf_from_meff}. Under \eqref{eq:z0_positive_assump},
the denominator does not alter the sign, hence
\[
\operatorname{sgn}\mu_\infty
=
\operatorname{sgn}\!\bigl(m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)\bigr).
\]
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Earliest reject criterion]
Under \eqref{eq:z0_positive_assump}, if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)\le 0,
}
\label{eq:earliest_reject_cond}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty\le 0,
}
\end{equation}
so the branch is rejected before any insertion of \(g_E\), \(g_c\), \(\kappa_*\), or competitor exclusion.
\end{corollary}

\section{3. Case decomposition of the asymptotic sign audit}

The sign reduction theorem is exact but abstract.
To make it executable, we separate the asymptotic sign patterns.

\subsection*{Case A: \(u_X(\sigma_\infty)\ge 0\) and \(\chi_\infty\ge 0\)}

Then the Class II correction lowers the bulk gap:
\begin{equation}
-\,3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)\le 0.
\end{equation}
Therefore one needs the sharp lower bound
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m(\sigma_\infty) > 3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)\ge 0.
}
\label{eq:mu_case_A}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{Case B: \(u_X(\sigma_\infty)\le 0\) and \(\chi_\infty\ge 0\)}

Then the correction helps the gap:
\begin{equation}
-\,3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)\ge 0.
\end{equation}
Hence the positivity condition becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m(\sigma_\infty) > 3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty),
}
\label{eq:mu_case_B}
\end{equation}
which is weaker than the naive sufficient requirement \(m(\sigma_\infty)>0\).

\subsection*{Case C: sign-indefinite asymptotic sector}

If the signs of \(\chi_\infty\) and \(u_X(\sigma_\infty)\) are not known a priori, then there is no further universal simplification.
However, the sign audit is still finite:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{sgn}\mu_\infty
=
\operatorname{sgn}\!\Bigl(m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)\Bigr),
\qquad
\text{assuming } z_0(\sigma_\infty)>0.
}
\label{eq:mu_case_C}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Benchmark-normalized accept/reject form}

The bulk decision can now be written in a completely executable form.

\begin{theorem}[Executable bulk accept/reject criterion]
Assume
\begin{equation}
z_0(\sigma_\infty)>0.
\end{equation}
Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_\mu
:=
m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty).
}
\label{eq:Delta_mu_def}
\end{equation}
Then exactly one of the following holds:
\begin{enumerate}
\item if \(\Delta_\mu>0\), then
\[
\mu_\infty>0
\]
and the branch passes the bulk positivity gate;

\item if \(\Delta_\mu=0\), then
\[
\mu_\infty=0
\]
and the branch is gapless at infinity, so the bulk positivity gate fails;

\item if \(\Delta_\mu<0\), then
\[
\mu_\infty<0
\]
and the branch is rejected immediately.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Immediate from
\[
\mu_\infty=\frac{\Delta_\mu}{z_0(\sigma_\infty)}
\]
with \(z_0(\sigma_\infty)>0\).
\end{proof}

\section{5. Relation to the full one-defect acceptance chain}

The full one-defect acceptance data are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(g_c,\ g_E,\ g_O,\ \mu_\infty,\ \kappa_*).
}
\end{equation}
But the correct finite audit order is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty
\;\longrightarrow\;
g_E
\;\longrightarrow\;
g_c
\;\longrightarrow\;
\kappa_*
\;\longrightarrow\;
\text{competitor exclusion}.
}
\end{equation}

Therefore the present bulk reduction is logically prior to all transport insertions.
If the bulk sign fails, then the rest of the one-defect audit is irrelevant for acceptance.

\section{6. Honest closure statement}

What is now fully closed is the \emph{structural} reduction of the bulk sign problem:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty
\text{ is completely controlled by the finite scalar set }
\{m(\sigma_\infty),u_X(\sigma_\infty),\chi_\infty,z_0(\sigma_\infty)\}.
}
\end{equation}

What is not yet inserted numerically or branch-specifically is the actual asymptotic evaluation of those four scalars on the chosen vacuum-asymptotic branch.

Hence the honest status is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{bulk positivity is no longer conceptually open,}
}
\end{equation}
but
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{it is not yet numerically closed until the chosen branch data are inserted.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

At the current C4 / one-defect acceptance stage, the bulk gate is the first and cheapest decisive test.

The asymptotic bulk mass parameter is
\[
\mu_\infty
=
\frac{m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)}{z_0(\sigma_\infty)}.
\]

Therefore, assuming
\[
z_0(\sigma_\infty)>0,
\]
the sign of \(\mu_\infty\) is exactly the sign of
\[
\Delta_\mu:=m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty).
\]

Hence:
\[
\Delta_\mu>0 \iff \mu_\infty>0,
\qquad
\Delta_\mu=0 \iff \mu_\infty=0,
\qquad
\Delta_\mu<0 \iff \mu_\infty<0.
\]

So the \(\mu_\infty\) problem is completely reduced to a finite four-scalar audit:
\[
m(\sigma_\infty),\qquad
u_X(\sigma_\infty),\qquad
\chi_\infty,\qquad
z_0(\sigma_\infty).
\]

This closes the structural bulk-sign problem.

What remains is not conceptual.
It is the explicit insertion of the chosen vacuum-asymptotic branch data into those four scalars.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Bulk Gate Closure on the Simplest Vacuum Branch and Transition to the \texorpdfstring{$g_E$}{gE} Audit}

\section{1. Priority order and bulk data}

The one-defect acceptance problem has already been reduced to a finite audit of
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(g_c,\ g_E,\ g_O,\ \mu_\infty,\ \kappa_*),
}
\end{equation}
with the correct priority order
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty
\;\longrightarrow\;
g_E
\;\longrightarrow\;
g_c
\;\longrightarrow\;
\kappa_*
\;\longrightarrow\;
\text{competitor exclusion}.
}
\end{equation}

The bulk package is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m(\sigma_\infty),\qquad
u_X(\sigma_\infty),\qquad
\chi_\infty,\qquad
z_0(\sigma_\infty).
}
\end{equation}

The exact constitutive bulk coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty
=
\frac{
m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)
}{
z_0(\sigma_\infty)
}.
}
\label{eq:mu_bulk_exact_again}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Exact sign reduction}

Assume the standard normalization
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
z_0(\sigma_\infty)>0.
}
\label{eq:z0_positive_again}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty>0
\iff
m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)>0.
}
\label{eq:mu_sign_general_again}
\end{equation}

Thus the general non-vacuum asymptotic branch requires the finite scalar comparison
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m(\sigma_\infty)>3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty).
}
\label{eq:general_nonvacuum_bulk}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Simplest vacuum branch}

Now specialize to the simplest vacuum branch. By definition,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
X_{\perp,\infty}=X_{\parallel,\infty}=0.
}
\label{eq:simplest_vacuum_branch}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\chi_\infty
=
\frac13\bigl(2X_{\perp,\infty}+X_{\parallel,\infty}\bigr)
=
0.
}
\label{eq:chi_infty_zero}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:chi_infty_zero} into \eqref{eq:mu_bulk_exact_again} gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty
=
\frac{m(\sigma_\infty)}{z_0(\sigma_\infty)}.
}
\label{eq:mu_vacuum_exact}
\end{equation}

Therefore, under \eqref{eq:z0_positive_again},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty>0
\iff
m(\sigma_\infty)>0.
}
\label{eq:mu_vacuum_sign_exact}
\end{equation}

\begin{theorem}[Bulk-gate closure on the simplest vacuum branch]
Assume the asymptotic branch satisfies
\[
X_{\perp,\infty}=X_{\parallel,\infty}=0,
\qquad
z_0(\sigma_\infty)>0.
\]
Then the one-defect bulk positivity gate is completely determined by the single scalar sign
\[
m(\sigma_\infty).
\]
More precisely,
\[
m(\sigma_\infty)>0
\iff
\mu_\infty>0,
\]
\[
m(\sigma_\infty)=0
\iff
\mu_\infty=0,
\]
\[
m(\sigma_\infty)<0
\iff
\mu_\infty<0.
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Immediate from \eqref{eq:mu_vacuum_exact}.
\end{proof}

\section{4. Honest logical consequence}

This is stronger than the generic non-vacuum statement.

On a general asymptotic Class-II branch,
the bulk gate requires the balance
\[
m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)>0.
\]
But on the simplest vacuum branch,
the Class-II asymptotic correction disappears identically:
\[
\chi_\infty=0.
\]
Therefore the bulk gate is no longer a balance problem.
It is a one-sign problem.

Hence, once the chosen working branch is the simplest vacuum branch,
the bulk frontier is effectively closed up to the sign of \(m(\sigma_\infty)\).

\section{5. Transition to the first real transport frontier}

After the bulk gate, the next audit is \(g_E\).

For the shell-projected transport coefficients,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=C_E g_E,
\qquad
\beta=C_O g_O.
}
\label{eq:alpha_beta_dictionary}
\end{equation}

In the explicit pure-even canonical realization,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
\alpha
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta=0.
}
\label{eq:explicit_pure_even_sheet}
\end{equation}

If, in addition, one adopts the canonical normalization
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_\parallel=C_E=C_O=1,
}
\label{eq:canonical_normalization_again}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_E=\alpha
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
g_O=0.
}
\label{eq:gE_sign_ready}
\end{equation}

Therefore the explicit pure-even canonical branch satisfies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_E>0
\iff
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,\theta_0\kappa>0.
}
\label{eq:gE_sign_ready_final}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Combined practical criterion after bulk closure}

In the practical lowest-channel case,
the explicit branch criterion is already reduced to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}
\right|
<
\frac{32}{3|\alpha_X|(\theta_0\kappa)^2},
\qquad
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0\kappa>0,
\qquad
\mu_\infty>0,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:four_checks_again}
\end{equation}

On the simplest vacuum branch, the third inequality becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m(\sigma_\infty)>0
\qquad
\text{(assuming }z_0(\sigma_\infty)>0\text{).}
}
\label{eq:four_checks_vacuum}
\end{equation}

So the practical explicit one-defect audit on this branch becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}
\right|
<
\frac{32}{3|\alpha_X|(\theta_0\kappa)^2},
\qquad
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0\kappa>0,
\qquad
m(\sigma_\infty)>0,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:four_checks_vacuum_final}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Honest status}

What is now closed:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the bulk sign problem is completely reduced;
\item on the simplest vacuum branch, it collapses to the single scalar sign \(m(\sigma_\infty)\);
\item the next genuine frontier is \(g_E\), not \(\mu_\infty\).
\end{enumerate}

What remains open explicitly:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the actual sign of \(m(\sigma_\infty)\) in the chosen TECT working branch;
\item the actual sign of \(\beta_X\theta_0\kappa\);
\item the longitudinal burden ratio through \(\xi_c/\xi_E\);
\item the final remote-gap numerical insertion.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Final Summary}

The bulk coefficient of the one-defect acceptance theorem is
\[
\mu_\infty
=
\frac{
m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)
}{
z_0(\sigma_\infty)
}.
\]

Under the standard normalization \(z_0(\sigma_\infty)>0\),
this is equivalent to
\[
\mu_\infty>0
\iff
m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)>0.
\]

However, on the simplest vacuum branch,
\[
X_{\perp,\infty}=X_{\parallel,\infty}=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\chi_\infty=0,
\]
so the bulk gate simplifies to
\[
\boxed{
\mu_\infty
=
\frac{m(\sigma_\infty)}{z_0(\sigma_\infty)},
\qquad
\mu_\infty>0
\iff
m(\sigma_\infty)>0.
}
\]

Thus the asymptotic Class-II correction disappears entirely at infinity on this branch.

Therefore the bulk frontier is no longer a balance problem.
It is a one-sign problem.

After this reduction, the first genuine remaining transport frontier is \(g_E\).
In the explicit pure-even canonical branch,
\[
\alpha
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta=0,
\]
so, under canonical normalization,
\[
\boxed{
g_E>0
\iff
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0\kappa>0.
}
\]

Hence the practical explicit one-defect audit on the simplest vacuum branch is
\[
\boxed{
\left|
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}
\right|
<
\frac{32}{3|\alpha_X|(\theta_0\kappa)^2},
\qquad
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0\kappa>0,
\qquad
m(\sigma_\infty)>0,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Explicit \texorpdfstring{$g_E$}{gE} Sign Audit and the Final Practical Acceptance Formula}

\section{Goal}

We now complete the \(g_E\)-sign audit on the explicit pure-even canonical branch
and combine it with the already reduced \(R_c\)-window and bulk sign condition.

The point is to pass from the abstract operational criterion
to a concrete branch-level constitutive criterion.

\section{1. Operational one-defect criterion}

The practical lowest-channel one-defect/one-mode criterion is already reduced to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-1<R_c<1,
\qquad
\alpha>0,
\qquad
\mu_\infty>0,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho},
}
\label{eq:operational_criterion_start}
\end{equation}
provided the projected lowest signed channel is unique and the competitors are spectrally excluded.

Equivalently, before introducing \(R_c\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty>0,
\qquad
\xi_E g_E+\xi_c g_c>0,
\qquad
\xi_E g_E>0,
\qquad
2|\kappa_*|\,\xi_E g_E>\xi_E g_E+\xi_c g_c.
}
\label{eq:preRc_operational}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Explicit branch data}

Fix the explicit canonical pure-even branch
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
T_\star=T^1,
\qquad
\gamma_E=1,
\qquad
\gamma_O=0,
\qquad
C_\parallel=C_E=C_O=1.
}
\label{eq:explicit_pure_even_branch}
\end{equation}

Then the extracted transport/Bloch coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c
=
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:gc_explicit}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_E
=
\alpha
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
g_O=0.
}
\label{eq:gE_explicit}
\end{equation}

Hence the odd transport sector drops out of the protected-channel counting problem.

\section{3. Exact \texorpdfstring{$g_E$}{gE} sign audit}

Since the prefactor
\[
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}>0,
\qquad
M_X^2>0,
\]
the sign of \(g_E\) is exactly the sign of
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:gE_sign_driver}
\end{equation}

Therefore:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_E>0
\iff
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0\kappa>0.
}
\label{eq:gE_sign_exact}
\end{equation}

Under the standard matching convention \(\xi_E>0\), this is also equivalent to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\xi_E g_E>0.
}
\label{eq:xiEgE_positive}
\end{equation}

So the transverse support test is no longer abstract.
It is a one-sign constitutive test.

\section{4. Exact longitudinal burden ratio}

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_c:=\frac{\xi_c g_c}{\xi_E g_E}.
}
\label{eq:Rc_def_again}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:gc_explicit} and \eqref{eq:gE_explicit} gives
\begin{align}
R_c
&=
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}
\frac{
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0^3\kappa^3
}{
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0\kappa
}
\nonumber\\[1ex]
&=
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}
\frac{3}{32}\,
\alpha_X\,
(\theta_0\kappa)^2.
\end{align}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_c
=
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\frac{3}{32}\alpha_X(\theta_0\kappa)^2.
}
\label{eq:Rc_explicit_exact}
\end{equation}

This already shows an important simplification:
the sign and size of the longitudinal burden are controlled by
\[
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\alpha_X
\]
and the defect amplitude only through the square \((\theta_0\kappa)^2\).

\section{5. Simplest vacuum bulk branch}

Now specialize the asymptotic constitutive branch further to the simplest vacuum branch:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\chi_\infty=0.
}
\label{eq:chi_zero_again}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty
=
\frac{m(\sigma_\infty)}{z_0(\sigma_\infty)}.
}
\label{eq:mu_simple_vacuum_again}
\end{equation}

Assuming the standard normalization
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
z_0(\sigma_\infty)>0,
}
\label{eq:z0_positive_again2}
\end{equation}
one gets the exact equivalence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty>0
\iff
m(\sigma_\infty)>0.
}
\label{eq:mu_simple_vacuum_sign}
\end{equation}

Thus the bulk sign gate is reduced to a single constitutive sign.

\section{6. Final practical theorem}

We now combine
\eqref{eq:operational_criterion_start},
\eqref{eq:gE_sign_exact},
\eqref{eq:Rc_explicit_exact},
and \eqref{eq:mu_simple_vacuum_sign}.

\begin{theorem}[Practical one-defect acceptance on the explicit pure-even canonical branch]
Assume:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the working branch is
\[
T_\star=T^1,\qquad \gamma_E=1,\qquad \gamma_O=0,
\qquad C_\parallel=C_E=C_O=1;
\]
\item the asymptotic constitutive branch is the simplest vacuum branch \(\chi_\infty=0\);
\item \(z_0(\sigma_\infty)>0\);
\item the projected low-slot structure is the practical lowest-channel case,
with a unique signed lowest channel and the standard competitor pattern;
\item the remote-gap condition
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
\]
holds.
\end{enumerate}
Then a sufficient practical acceptance criterion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m(\sigma_\infty)>0,
\qquad
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0\kappa>0,
\qquad
\left|
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\frac{3}{32}\alpha_X(\theta_0\kappa)^2
\right|<1,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:final_practical_four}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The operational criterion requires
\[
-1<R_c<1,\qquad \alpha>0,\qquad \mu_\infty>0,
\qquad \Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
\]
Using \eqref{eq:gE_explicit},
\[
\alpha>0
\iff
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0\kappa>0.
\]
Using \eqref{eq:Rc_explicit_exact},
\[
-1<R_c<1
\iff
\left|
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\frac{3}{32}\alpha_X(\theta_0\kappa)^2
\right|<1.
\]
Using \eqref{eq:mu_simple_vacuum_sign},
\[
\mu_\infty>0
\iff
m(\sigma_\infty)>0.
\]
Combining these with the remote-gap condition yields \eqref{eq:final_practical_four}.
\end{proof}

\section{7. Small-defect corollary}

If
\[
\left|\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\alpha_X\right|
\]
is \(O(1)\) and \(|\theta_0\kappa|\ll 1\),
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_c
=
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\frac{3}{32}\alpha_X(\theta_0\kappa)^2
}
\end{equation}
is automatically small, hence the \(R_c\)-window is naturally satisfied.

So in the small-defect regime the genuinely nontrivial constitutive tests are primarily:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m(\sigma_\infty)>0,
\qquad
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0\kappa>0,
}
\end{equation}
while the longitudinal burden inequality becomes mild.

\section{8. Sharpened sign cases for \texorpdfstring{$R_c$}{Rc}}

Because \((\theta_0\kappa)^2\ge 0\), the sign of \(R_c\) is the sign of
\[
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\alpha_X.
\]

Hence:

\paragraph{Case A: \(\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\alpha_X>0\).}
Then \(R_c\ge 0\), so the lower bound \(R_c>-1\) is automatic.
Only the upper bound matters:
\[
\boxed{
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\frac{3}{32}\alpha_X(\theta_0\kappa)^2<1.
}
\]

\paragraph{Case B: \(\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\alpha_X<0\).}
Then \(R_c\le 0\), so the upper bound \(R_c<1\) is automatic.
Only the lower bound matters:
\[
\boxed{
\left|
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\frac{3}{32}\alpha_X(\theta_0\kappa)^2
\right|<1.
}
\]

Thus the absolute-value form is the cleanest universal formulation.

\section{9. Honest status}

What is now closed structurally and branch-explicitly:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(g_O=0\) on the explicit pure-even canonical branch;
\item \(g_E\)-positivity is exactly the sign of \((\beta_X/M_X^2)\theta_0\kappa\);
\item \(g_c\) enters only through the explicit burden ratio
\[
R_c=\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\frac{3}{32}\alpha_X(\theta_0\kappa)^2;
\]
\item on the simplest vacuum branch, the bulk sign is exactly the sign of \(m(\sigma_\infty)\).
\end{enumerate}

Therefore the one-defect acceptance problem is no longer structurally open on this branch.
What remains is only the insertion of actual asymptotic constitutive data and the remote-gap bound.

\section{Final Summary}

On the explicit pure-even canonical branch
\[
T_\star=T^1,\qquad
\gamma_E=1,\qquad
\gamma_O=0,\qquad
C_\parallel=C_E=C_O=1,
\]
the transport coefficients are
\[
g_c
=
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
g_E
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
g_O=0.
\]

Hence the transverse support sign is exactly
\[
g_E>0
\iff
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0\kappa>0.
\]

The longitudinal burden ratio is explicitly
\[
R_c
=
\frac{\xi_c g_c}{\xi_E g_E}
=
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\frac{3}{32}\alpha_X(\theta_0\kappa)^2.
\]

On the simplest vacuum branch \(\chi_\infty=0\), one has
\[
\mu_\infty
=
\frac{m(\sigma_\infty)}{z_0(\sigma_\infty)},
\]
so, under \(z_0(\sigma_\infty)>0\),
\[
\mu_\infty>0
\iff
m(\sigma_\infty)>0.
\]

Therefore the practical one-defect acceptance criterion reduces to
\[
\boxed{
m(\sigma_\infty)>0,
\qquad
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0\kappa>0,
\qquad
\left|
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\frac{3}{32}\alpha_X(\theta_0\kappa)^2
\right|<1,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\]

So the explicit branch has now collapsed to:

\begin{itemize}
\item three constitutive checks,
\item plus one spectral isolation check.
\end{itemize}

No additional structural derivation is required at this stage.
The remaining frontier is only the finite insertion of actual branch data.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Executable Accept/Reject Sheet for the Explicit One-Defect Branch}

\section{Goal}

At the current stage, the one-defect acceptance problem is no longer conceptual.
It has already been reduced to a finite audit of
\[
(g_c,\ g_E,\ g_O,\ \mu_\infty,\ \kappa_*).
\]
The remaining task is therefore to write the final accept/reject sheet explicitly.

\section{1. Lowest-channel practical criterion}

In the practically relevant lowest-channel case, the sufficient one-defect criterion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-1<R_c<1,
\qquad
\alpha>0,
\qquad
\mu_\infty>0,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:lowest_four_checks}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, using
\[
R_c=\frac{\xi_c g_c}{\xi_E g_E},
\]
this is the reduced finite scalar form of the original core inequalities.

\section{2. Explicit canonical branch}

Fix the explicit canonical branch
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
T_\star=T^1,\qquad \gamma_E=1,\qquad \gamma_O=0.
}
\label{eq:explicit_branch}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c=\lambda_\parallel,
\qquad
g_E=\alpha,
\qquad
g_O=0.
}
\label{eq:explicit_gs}
\end{equation}

The explicit coefficient sheet gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c
=
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:gc_explicit_sheet}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_E
=
\alpha
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
g_O=0.
}
\label{eq:gE_explicit_sheet}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_c
=
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\frac{g_c}{g_E}
=
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\frac{3}{32}\alpha_X(\theta_0\kappa)^2.
}
\label{eq:Rc_explicit_sheet}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Bulk sign}

The exact bulk parameter is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty
=
\frac{
m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)
}{
z_0(\sigma_\infty)
}.
}
\label{eq:mu_general}
\end{equation}

Under the standard convention
\[
z_0(\sigma_\infty)>0,
\]
one has
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty>0
\iff
m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)>0.
}
\label{eq:mu_positive_general}
\end{equation}

If one further specializes to the simplest vacuum branch
\[
\chi_\infty=0,
\]
then this simplifies to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty>0
\iff
m(\sigma_\infty)>0.
}
\label{eq:mu_positive_vacuum}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Final executable decision sheet}

Combining \eqref{eq:lowest_four_checks}, \eqref{eq:gE_explicit_sheet},
\eqref{eq:Rc_explicit_sheet}, and \eqref{eq:mu_positive_vacuum}, one gets:

\begin{theorem}[Executable accept/reject sheet for the simplest explicit branch]
Assume:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the explicit canonical branch \eqref{eq:explicit_branch};
\item the simplest vacuum asymptotic branch \(\chi_\infty=0\);
\item \(z_0(\sigma_\infty)>0\);
\item the lowest-channel reduction is valid.
\end{enumerate}
Then a sufficient acceptance criterion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m(\sigma_\infty)>0,
\qquad
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0\kappa>0,
\qquad
\left|
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\frac{3}{32}\alpha_X(\theta_0\kappa)^2
\right|<1,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:final_accept_sheet}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The four checks in \eqref{eq:lowest_four_checks} are:
\begin{itemize}
\item \(\mu_\infty>0\), which becomes \(m(\sigma_\infty)>0\) on the simplest vacuum branch;
\item \(\alpha>0\), which becomes \((\beta_X/M_X^2)\theta_0\kappa>0\);
\item \(-1<R_c<1\), which becomes the absolute-value inequality in \eqref{eq:final_accept_sheet};
\item the remote-gap inequality.
\end{itemize}
This proves the result.
\end{proof}

\section{5. Immediate reject rules}

The same theorem yields the following immediate sufficient rejection rules.

\paragraph{Bulk reject.}
If
\[
m(\sigma_\infty)\le 0
\]
(on the simplest vacuum branch), then
\[
\mu_\infty\le 0,
\]
so the branch fails before any transport-side test.

\paragraph{Transverse-support reject.}
If
\[
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0\kappa\le 0,
\]
then
\[
g_E\le 0,
\]
so the lowest transverse support test fails.

\paragraph{Longitudinal-overload reject.}
If
\[
\left|
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\frac{3}{32}\alpha_X(\theta_0\kappa)^2
\right|\ge 1,
\]
then the longitudinal burden exceeds the allowed window.

\paragraph{Remote-sector reject.}
If
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}\le \eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho},
\]
then the enriched low slot is not spectrally isolated from the remote sector.

\section{6. Unit-benchmark corollary}

For the benchmark choice
\[
\alpha_X=\beta_X=M_X=\xi_E=\xi_c=z_{0,0}=1,
\]
one obtains
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_c=0.09375\,(\theta_0\kappa)^2.
}
\label{eq:unit_Rc}
\end{equation}

Hence:
\[
\theta_0\kappa=0.1 \Rightarrow R_c=9.375\times 10^{-4},
\]
\[
\theta_0\kappa=0.3 \Rightarrow R_c=8.4375\times 10^{-3},
\]
\[
\theta_0\kappa=1 \Rightarrow R_c=9.375\times 10^{-2}.
\]

Therefore, throughout the natural small-defect regime, the \(R_c\)-window is automatically mild.

\section{7. Honest structural caveat}

The preceding decision sheet uses the explicit pure-even coefficient identification
\[
g_E=\alpha
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0\kappa.
\]

However, the broader Schur-reduced working-branch formula can also be written as
\[
\alpha
=
I_\theta
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_E^{(0)}.
\]

Therefore the sign of \(g_E\) is fully branch-explicit only after fixing which branch normalization and coefficient dictionary is being used.
This does not reopen the structure of the proof,
but it does mean that the final numerical sign insertion is still branch-specific.

\section{8. Honest conclusion}

What is now fully closed:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the one-defect acceptance problem is reduced to four scalar checks;
\item the explicit decision sheet \eqref{eq:final_accept_sheet} is complete;
\item the reject modes are fully classified.
\end{enumerate}

What is still not fixed by the uploaded notes:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the actual branch values of \(m(\sigma_\infty)\);
\item the actual matching constants \(\xi_E,\xi_c\);
\item the actual remote-gap margin
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}-\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho};
\]
\item the final branch-normalization convention entering the sign of \(g_E\).
\end{enumerate}

So the remaining frontier is not theorem-building.
It is finite constitutive insertion.

\section{Final Summary}

The one-defect acceptance problem has already been reduced to the finite data
\[
(g_c,\ g_E,\ g_O,\ \mu_\infty,\ \kappa_*).
\]

On the explicit canonical branch
\[
T_\star=T^1,\qquad \gamma_E=1,\qquad \gamma_O=0,
\]
the lowest-channel practical criterion is
\[
-1<R_c<1,
\qquad
\alpha>0,
\qquad
\mu_\infty>0,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
\]

Using the explicit coefficient sheet,
\[
g_c
=
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
g_E
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
g_O=0,
\]
so
\[
R_c
=
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\frac{3}{32}\alpha_X(\theta_0\kappa)^2.
\]

Moreover,
\[
\mu_\infty
=
\frac{m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)}{z_0(\sigma_\infty)},
\]
and on the simplest vacuum branch \(\chi_\infty=0\) with \(z_0(\sigma_\infty)>0\),
\[
\mu_\infty>0
\iff
m(\sigma_\infty)>0.
\]

Therefore the explicit accept/reject sheet is
\[
\boxed{
m(\sigma_\infty)>0,
\qquad
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0\kappa>0,
\qquad
\left|
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\frac{3}{32}\alpha_X(\theta_0\kappa)^2
\right|<1,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\]

This is the fully reduced practical criterion.

However, the uploaded notes still do not fix the actual branch values of
\[
m(\sigma_\infty),\qquad
\xi_E,\qquad
\xi_c,\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}-\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho},
\]
nor do they completely eliminate the branch-normalization ambiguity in the final sign dictionary for \(g_E\).

Hence the remaining frontier is finite constitutive insertion, not new theorem-building.

\section{Normalization-Aware Exact Pass Certificate for Gate 5}

\section{Goal}

We continue the current line up to its actual termination point.

The correct endpoint is not another auxiliary reformulation.
It is the exact normalization-aware reduction of the post-acceptance one-defect test
to a finite set of branch scalars that can be directly inserted on the intended Class II branch.

\section{1. Exact one-defect core criterion}

The one-defect theorem is controlled by
\[
(g_c,\ g_E,\ g_O,\ \mu_\infty,\ \kappa_*),
\]
with core coefficients
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_0=\frac{\xi_E g_E+\xi_c g_c}{z_{0,0}},
\qquad
b_0=\frac{\xi_E g_E}{z_{0,0}},
\qquad
c_0=\frac{\xi_O g_O}{z_{0,0}}.
}
\label{eq:a0b0c0_exact}
\end{equation}

The sufficient one-defect/one-mode criterion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty>0,
\qquad
a_0>0,
\qquad
b_0>0,
\qquad
\frac{|\kappa_*|\,b_0}{a_0}>\frac12.
}
\label{eq:one_mode_general}
\end{equation}

In the practically most relevant lowest-channel case
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\kappa_*|=1,
}
\label{eq:kappa_lowest}
\end{equation}
the decisive inequality becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\xi_E g_E>\xi_c g_c.
}
\label{eq:lowest_decisive}
\end{equation}

Assuming \(z_{0,0}>0\), \eqref{eq:one_mode_general} is equivalent to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty>0,
\qquad
\xi_E g_E>0,
\qquad
-1<R_{\mathrm{exact}}<1,
}
\label{eq:lowest_exact_reduction}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_{\mathrm{exact}}
:=
\frac{\xi_c g_c}{\xi_E g_E}.
}
\label{eq:Rexact_def}
\end{equation}

Finally, Gate 5 must be supported by the remote-gap support theorem:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{gap}}
:=
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}-\eta_{R,\rho}>0.
}
\label{eq:Dgap_def}
\end{equation}

Thus the exact post-acceptance Gate-5 problem is already reduced to four scalars:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_\mu,\qquad
S_E,\qquad
R_{\mathrm{exact}},\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{gap}},
}
\label{eq:four_exact_scalars}
\end{equation}
where
\[
\Delta_\mu:=m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty),
\qquad
S_E:=\xi_E g_E.
\]

\section{2. Exact normalization layer}

The exact reduced coefficient dictionary is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:red_dict}
\end{equation}
Together with the exact overlap-normalization law
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c=\frac{\lambda_\parallel}{C_c},
\qquad
g_E=\frac{\alpha}{C_E},
\qquad
g_O=\frac{\beta}{C_O},
}
\label{eq:norm_dict}
\end{equation}
this gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c=\frac{I_{\theta'^3}}{2C_c}\lambda_c,
\qquad
g_E=\frac{I_\theta}{C_E}\Lambda_E,
\qquad
g_O=\frac{I_\theta}{C_O}\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:g_from_lambdaLambda}
\end{equation}

Therefore the transverse sign scalar is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_E
=
\xi_E g_E
=
\xi_E\frac{I_\theta}{C_E}\Lambda_E.
}
\label{eq:SE_exact}
\end{equation}

Likewise,
\begin{equation}
R_{\mathrm{exact}}
=
\frac{\xi_c g_c}{\xi_E g_E}
=
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}
\frac{C_E}{C_c}
\frac{I_{\theta'^3}}{2I_\theta}
\frac{\lambda_c}{\Lambda_E}.
\label{eq:Rexact_first}
\end{equation}

Using
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}=-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:Itheta_vals}
\end{equation}
one obtains
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{I_{\theta'^3}}{2I_\theta}
=
\frac{3}{32}(\theta_0\kappa)^2.
}
\label{eq:Iratio_exact}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_{\mathrm{exact}}
=
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}
\frac{C_E}{C_c}
\frac{3}{32}(\theta_0\kappa)^2
\frac{\lambda_c}{\Lambda_E}.
}
\label{eq:Rexact_closed}
\end{equation}

This is the exact normalization-aware longitudinal burden ratio.
It is the correct endpoint of the current line,
because it removes all earlier convention-dependent ambiguity.

\section{3. Bulk scalar}

The exact bulk mass parameter is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{

=

\label{eq:Delta_mu_vac}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Working-branch source packages}

The current working-branch scalar reductions are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E
=
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,\mathfrak T_E,

\Lambda_O
=

|G_*|\,
A_{G_*}.

Therefore

\frac{\alpha_X}{\beta_X}
\frac{
\mathcal N_{JJ}m_\parallel u_\parallel |G_*|A_{G_*}
}{
\mathfrak T_E
}.

Equation \eqref{eq:Rexact_package} is not a new theorem;

Assume:

\section{Exact Sign Audit for \texorpdfstring{$\Delta_\mu$}{Delta_mu} and \texorpdfstring{$S_E$}{S_E}}

\section{Goal}

Inside the current one-defect acceptance line, the exact finite audit has already been reduced to
\[
(\Delta_\mu,\ S_E,\ R_{\mathrm{exact}},\ \Delta_{\mathrm{gap}}).
\]
In this section we close the first two sign problems:
\[
\Delta_\mu
=
m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty),
\qquad
S_E
=
\xi_E g_E.
\]

\section{1. Bulk sign scalar \texorpdfstring{$\Delta_\mu$}{Delta_mu}}

The exact bulk mass parameter is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty
=
\frac{
m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)
}{
z_0(\sigma_\infty)
}
=
\frac{\Delta_\mu}{z_0(\sigma_\infty)}.
}
\label{eq:muinf_delta_exact}
\end{equation}

Assume the standard sign convention
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
z_0(\sigma_\infty)>0.
}
\label{eq:z0_positive_signaudit}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty>0
\iff
\Delta_\mu>0.
}
\label{eq:mu_delta_equiv}
\end{equation}

Therefore the exact bulk sign table is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_\mu>0
\iff
\mu_\infty>0,
\qquad
\Delta_\mu=0
\iff
\mu_\infty=0,
\qquad
\Delta_\mu<0
\iff
\mu_\infty<0.
}
\label{eq:bulk_signtable_exact}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Branch-resolved cases}

Because
\[
\Delta_\mu=m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty),
\]
there are three honest asymptotic sign patterns.

\paragraph{Case A: \(u_X(\sigma_\infty)\ge 0\), \(\chi_\infty\ge 0\).}
Then the Class-II correction reduces the bulk gap, and one needs
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m(\sigma_\infty)>3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)\ge 0.
}
\label{eq:Delta_mu_caseA}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Case B: \(u_X(\sigma_\infty)\le 0\), \(\chi_\infty\ge 0\).}
Then the correction helps the bulk gap, so the exact condition is only
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m(\sigma_\infty)>3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty),
}
\label{eq:Delta_mu_caseB}
\end{equation}
which is weaker than \(m(\sigma_\infty)>0\).

\paragraph{Case C: sign-indefinite asymptotic branch.}
Then there is no further universal simplification:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{sgn}\Delta_\mu
=
\operatorname{sgn}\!\Bigl(
m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:Delta_mu_caseC}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Simplest vacuum branch}

If the intended asymptotic branch is the simplest vacuum branch,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\chi_\infty=0,
}
\label{eq:chi_infty_zero_branch}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_\mu=m(\sigma_\infty),
\qquad
\mu_\infty>0\iff m(\sigma_\infty)>0.
}
\label{eq:Delta_mu_simplestvac}
\end{equation}

So on that branch the bulk gate is no longer a balance problem.
It is a one-sign problem.

\section{2. Transverse support scalar \texorpdfstring{$S_E$}{S_E}}

The exact normalization layer is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
g_E=\frac{\alpha}{C_E}.
}
\label{eq:alpha_gE_exact}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_E
:=
\xi_E g_E
=
\xi_E\frac{I_\theta}{C_E}\Lambda_E.
}
\label{eq:SE_def_exact}
\end{equation}

For Branch B the exact overlap coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:Itheta_branchB}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_E
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{\xi_E}{C_E}\,
\theta_0\kappa\,
\Lambda_E.
}
\label{eq:SE_branchB_exact}
\end{equation}

Since \(\sqrt3\pi/16>0\), the exact sign law is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{sgn}S_E
=
-\operatorname{sgn}\!\Bigl(
\frac{\xi_E}{C_E}\,
\theta_0\kappa\,
\Lambda_E
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:SE_sign_exact}
\end{equation}

Thus the exact sign table is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\xi_E}{C_E}\theta_0\kappa\Lambda_E<0
\iff S_E>0,
}
\label{eq:SE_positive_table}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\xi_E}{C_E}\theta_0\kappa\Lambda_E=0
\iff S_E=0,
}
\label{eq:SE_zero_table}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\xi_E}{C_E}\theta_0\kappa\Lambda_E>0
\iff S_E<0.
}
\label{eq:SE_negative_table}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Working-branch package for \texorpdfstring{$S_E$}{S_E}}

The transverse branch-level reduced package is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E
=
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,\mathfrak T_E.
}
\label{eq:LambdaE_package}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:LambdaE_package} into \eqref{eq:SE_branchB_exact} gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_E
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{\xi_E}{C_E}\,
\theta_0\kappa\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\mathfrak T_E.
}
\label{eq:SE_package_exact}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{sgn}S_E
=
-\operatorname{sgn}\!\Bigl(
\frac{\xi_E}{C_E}\,
\theta_0\kappa\,
\alpha_X\beta_X\,
\mathfrak T_E
\Bigr),
}
\label{eq:SE_package_sign}
\end{equation}
since \(M_X^2>0\) does not affect the sign.

Therefore the transverse sign problem is fully reduced to the finite sign audit of
\[
\xi_E,\qquad C_E,\qquad \theta_0\kappa,\qquad \alpha_X,\qquad \beta_X,\qquad \mathfrak T_E.
\]

\section{4. Explicit pure-even working realization}

There is also a sharper practical witness realization:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta=0.
}
\label{eq:alpha_pureeven_realization}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_E=\frac{\alpha}{C_E}
=
\frac{1}{C_E}
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:gE_pureeven_realization}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_E
=
\frac{\xi_E}{C_E}
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:SE_pureeven_realization}
\end{equation}

Hence the practical sign law on this explicit pure-even realization is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{sgn}S_E
=
\operatorname{sgn}\!\Bigl(
\frac{\xi_E}{C_E}\,
\beta_X\,
\theta_0\kappa
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:SE_pureeven_sign}
\end{equation}

In the canonical practical choice
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_E=1,
\qquad
\xi_E>0,
}
\label{eq:canonical_sign_choice}
\end{equation}
this collapses to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_E>0
\iff
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0\kappa>0.
}
\label{eq:SE_pureeven_final}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Honest relation between the two sign formulas}

The formulas \eqref{eq:SE_sign_exact} and \eqref{eq:SE_pureeven_sign} are not contradictory.
They correspond to two different insertion levels:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the exact normalization-aware overlap formula, written in terms of \(\Lambda_E\);
\item the practical explicit pure-even witness realization, where the branch-specific sign of \(\Lambda_E\) has already been absorbed into the chosen realization.
\end{enumerate}

Therefore the exact sign driver is always \(\Lambda_E\), but the practical explicit pure-even witness may reduce this further to the simpler \(\beta_X\theta_0\kappa\) sign test.

\section{6. Partial Gate-5 certificate now obtained}

At this stage, the first two exact sign audits are completely reduced:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_\mu>0
\iff
m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)>0
\qquad
(z_0(\sigma_\infty)>0),
}
\label{eq:partial_gate5_1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_E>0
\iff
-\frac{\xi_E}{C_E}\theta_0\kappa\Lambda_E>0,
}
\label{eq:partial_gate5_2}
\end{equation}
or at the working-branch package level,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_E>0
\iff
-\frac{\xi_E}{C_E}\theta_0\kappa
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\mathfrak T_E
>0.
}
\label{eq:partial_gate5_2_package}
\end{equation}

On the simplest vacuum + explicit pure-even practical realization, these become
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m(\sigma_\infty)>0,
\qquad
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0\kappa>0
\quad
(C_E=1,\ \xi_E>0).
}
\label{eq:partial_gate5_pureeven_vacuum}
\end{equation}

Thus the remaining Gate-5 work inside the current line is only:
\[
R_{\mathrm{exact}}
\quad\text{and}\quad
\Delta_{\mathrm{gap}}.
\]

\section{Final Summary}

The first two exact sign variables of the current Gate-5 finite audit are
\[
\Delta_\mu
=
m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty),
\qquad
S_E
=
\xi_E g_E.
\]

The bulk sign is exact:
\[
\mu_\infty
=
\frac{\Delta_\mu}{z_0(\sigma_\infty)}.
\]
Hence, under \(z_0(\sigma_\infty)>0\),
\[
\boxed{
\mu_\infty>0
\iff
\Delta_\mu>0.
}
\]

On the simplest vacuum branch \(\chi_\infty=0\),
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_\mu=m(\sigma_\infty),
\qquad
\mu_\infty>0\iff m(\sigma_\infty)>0.
}
\]

For the transverse support scalar,
\[
S_E
=
\xi_E\frac{I_\theta}{C_E}\Lambda_E,
\qquad
I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa,
\]
so
\[
\boxed{
S_E
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}
\frac{\xi_E}{C_E}
\theta_0\kappa
\Lambda_E.
}
\]
Therefore
\[
\boxed{
S_E>0
\iff
\frac{\xi_E}{C_E}\theta_0\kappa\Lambda_E<0.
}
\]

At the working-branch package level,
\[
\Lambda_E=\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\mathfrak T_E,
\]
hence
\[
\boxed{
S_E>0
\iff
\frac{\xi_E}{C_E}\theta_0\kappa\alpha_X\beta_X\mathfrak T_E<0.
}
\]

On the explicit pure-even practical realization,
\[
\alpha
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta=0,
\]
so under \(C_E=1\) and \(\xi_E>0\),
\[
\boxed{
S_E>0
\iff
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0\kappa>0.
}
\]

Thus the current line has now reduced the first two Gate-5 sign problems completely.
Only the exact burden ratio \(R_{\mathrm{exact}}\) and the remote-gap margin \(\Delta_{\mathrm{gap}}\) remain.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Exact Sign/Size Audit for \texorpdfstring{$R_{\mathrm{exact}}$}{Rexact}}

\section{Goal}

Inside the current Gate-5 finite audit, only two items remain after the sign audits of
\[
\Delta_\mu
\quad\text{and}\quad
S_E.
\]
The next one is the exact longitudinal burden ratio
\[
R_{\mathrm{exact}}:=\frac{\xi_c g_c}{\xi_E g_E}.
\]

We now reduce it completely to a finite branch scalar audit.

\section{1. Exact normalization-aware formula}

The exact overlap dictionary is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}\lambda_c,
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O,
}
\label{eq:Rexact_dict1}
\end{equation}
together with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c=\frac{\lambda_\parallel}{C_c},
\qquad
g_E=\frac{\alpha}{C_E},
\qquad
g_O=\frac{\beta}{C_O}.
}
\label{eq:Rexact_dict2}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
g_c=\frac{I_{\theta'^3}}{2C_c}\lambda_c,
\qquad
g_E=\frac{I_\theta}{C_E}\Lambda_E.
\label{eq:Rexact_gcgE}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{align}
R_{\mathrm{exact}}
&=
\frac{\xi_c g_c}{\xi_E g_E}
\nonumber\\
&=
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}
\frac{
\frac{I_{\theta'^3}}{2C_c}\lambda_c
}{
\frac{I_\theta}{C_E}\Lambda_E
}
\nonumber\\
&=
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\frac{C_E}{C_c}
\frac{I_{\theta'^3}}{2I_\theta}
\frac{\lambda_c}{\Lambda_E}.
\label{eq:Rexact_pre_overlap}
\end{align}

Using the explicit defect overlaps
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
I_\theta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa,
}
\label{eq:Rexact_overlaps}
\end{equation}
one gets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{I_{\theta'^3}}{2I_\theta}
=
\frac{3}{32}(\theta_0\kappa)^2.
}
\label{eq:Rexact_overlap_ratio}
\end{equation}

Substituting this into \eqref{eq:Rexact_pre_overlap},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_{\mathrm{exact}}
=
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\frac{C_E}{C_c}
\frac{3}{32}(\theta_0\kappa)^2
\frac{\lambda_c}{\Lambda_E}.
}
\label{eq:Rexact_exact}
\end{equation}

This is the exact normalization-aware burden ratio.

\section{2. Exact sign law}

We work inside the already surviving transverse-support sector, so
\[
S_E=\xi_E g_E\neq 0
\qquad\Longrightarrow\qquad
\Lambda_E\neq 0.
\]
Then the sign of \(R_{\mathrm{exact}}\) is well-defined.

Since
\[
\frac{3}{32}>0,
\qquad
(\theta_0\kappa)^2\ge 0,
\]
the defect sign does not enter the sign of \(R_{\mathrm{exact}}\).
More precisely, for \(\theta_0\kappa\neq 0\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{sgn}R_{\mathrm{exact}}
=
\operatorname{sgn}\!\Bigl(
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\frac{C_E}{C_c}\frac{\lambda_c}{\Lambda_E}
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:Rexact_sign}
\end{equation}

Hence the exact sign table is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\frac{C_E}{C_c}\frac{\lambda_c}{\Lambda_E}>0
\iff
R_{\mathrm{exact}}>0,
}
\label{eq:Rexact_signtable_pos}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c=0
\iff
R_{\mathrm{exact}}=0
\qquad
(\Lambda_E\neq 0),
}
\label{eq:Rexact_signtable_zero}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\frac{C_E}{C_c}\frac{\lambda_c}{\Lambda_E}<0
\iff
R_{\mathrm{exact}}<0.
}
\label{eq:Rexact_signtable_neg}
\end{equation}

Thus the burden sign is controlled only by the relative sign of the longitudinal and transverse source packages, dressed by the matching/normalization factors.

\section{3. Exact size window}

In the practically relevant lowest-channel case, Gate 5 requires
\[
-1<R_{\mathrm{exact}}<1.
\]
Using \eqref{eq:Rexact_exact}, this is equivalent to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\frac{C_E}{C_c}
\frac{3}{32}(\theta_0\kappa)^2
\frac{\lambda_c}{\Lambda_E}
\right|<1.
}
\label{eq:Rexact_window_abs}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|\frac{\lambda_c}{\Lambda_E}\right|
<
\frac{32}{3}
\left|\frac{\xi_E}{\xi_c}\right|
\frac{C_c}{C_E}
\frac{1}{(\theta_0\kappa)^2}.
}
\label{eq:Rexact_window_ratio}
\end{equation}

So the exact burden window is a finite upper bound on the source ratio \(|\lambda_c/\Lambda_E|\).

\section{4. Automatic one-sided passes}

Equation \eqref{eq:Rexact_window_abs} immediately gives two useful one-sided reductions.

\paragraph{Case A: \(R_{\mathrm{exact}}\ge 0\).}
Then the lower bound \(R_{\mathrm{exact}}>-1\) is automatic, and Gate 5 only requires
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_{\mathrm{exact}}<1.
}
\label{eq:Rexact_caseA}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Case B: \(R_{\mathrm{exact}}\le 0\).}
Then the upper bound \(R_{\mathrm{exact}}<1\) is automatic, and Gate 5 only requires
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_{\mathrm{exact}}>-1.
}
\label{eq:Rexact_caseB}
\end{equation}

Thus the sign audit tells us which side of the window is nontrivial.

\section{5. Working-branch source insertion}

The current longitudinal finite scalar reduction gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c^{(JJ)}
\sim
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\,
\mathcal N_{JJ}\,
m_\parallel\,
u_\parallel\,
|G_*|A_{G_*},
}
\label{eq:Rexact_lambdacJJ}
\end{equation}
while the transverse branch-level package is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E
=
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,\mathfrak T_E.
}
\label{eq:Rexact_LambdaE}
\end{equation}

Therefore, at the current leading working-branch level,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\lambda_c}{\Lambda_E}
\sim
\frac{\alpha_X}{\beta_X}
\frac{
\mathcal N_{JJ}\,m_\parallel\,u_\parallel\,|G_*|A_{G_*}
}{
\mathfrak T_E
}.
}
\label{eq:Rexact_source_ratio}
\end{equation}

Substituting into \eqref{eq:Rexact_exact},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_{\mathrm{exact}}
\sim
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\frac{C_E}{C_c}
\frac{3}{32}(\theta_0\kappa)^2
\frac{\alpha_X}{\beta_X}
\frac{
\mathcal N_{JJ}\,m_\parallel\,u_\parallel\,|G_*|A_{G_*}
}{
\mathfrak T_E
}.
}
\label{eq:Rexact_working}
\end{equation}

Hence the exact sign law becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{sgn}R_{\mathrm{exact}}
=
\operatorname{sgn}\!\Bigl(
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\frac{C_E}{C_c}
\frac{\alpha_X}{\beta_X}
\frac{
\mathcal N_{JJ}\,m_\parallel\,u_\parallel\,|G_*|A_{G_*}
}{
\mathfrak T_E
}
\Bigr),
}
\label{eq:Rexact_working_sign}
\end{equation}
and the exact size window becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\frac{C_E}{C_c}
\frac{3}{32}(\theta_0\kappa)^2
\frac{\alpha_X}{\beta_X}
\frac{
\mathcal N_{JJ}\,m_\parallel\,u_\parallel\,|G_*|A_{G_*}
}{
\mathfrak T_E
}
\right|
<1.
}
\label{eq:Rexact_working_window}
\end{equation}

So the longitudinal frontier is fully reduced to the finite sign/size audit of
\[
\mathcal N_{JJ},\quad
m_\parallel,\quad
u_\parallel,\quad
A_{G_*},\quad
\mathfrak T_E,
\quad
\text{and the calibration constants }C_c,C_E,\xi_c,\xi_E.
\]

\section{6. Explicit practical specialization}

In the practical explicit branch summary, the burden was already reduced to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_c
=
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\frac{3}{32}\alpha_X(\theta_0\kappa)^2,
}
\label{eq:Rexact_practical}
\end{equation}
with the acceptance window
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\right|
<
\frac{32}{3|\alpha_X|(\theta_0\kappa)^2}.
}
\label{eq:Rexact_practical_window}
\end{equation}

This is precisely the specialization of the exact formula \eqref{eq:Rexact_exact}
to the explicit branch-level normalization choice in which the source ratio
\[
\frac{C_E}{C_c}\frac{\lambda_c}{\Lambda_E}
\]
collapses to \(\alpha_X\).

\section{7. Partial Gate-5 certificate after the third audit}

At this point, three of the four Gate-5 slots are completely reduced:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_\mu>0
\iff
m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)>0
\qquad
(z_0(\sigma_\infty)>0),
}
\label{eq:Gate5_slot1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_E>0
\iff
-\frac{\xi_E}{C_E}\theta_0\kappa\Lambda_E>0,
}
\label{eq:Gate5_slot2}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-1<R_{\mathrm{exact}}<1
\iff
\left|
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\frac{C_E}{C_c}
\frac{3}{32}(\theta_0\kappa)^2
\frac{\lambda_c}{\Lambda_E}
\right|<1.
}
\label{eq:Gate5_slot3}
\end{equation}

Therefore only the support-theorem side remains:
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{gap}}
=
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}-\eta_{R,\rho}.
\]

No additional structural work remains inside the present line beyond that final support insertion.

\section{Final Summary}

The exact normalization-aware longitudinal burden ratio is
\[
R_{\mathrm{exact}}
=
\frac{\xi_c g_c}{\xi_E g_E}
=
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\frac{C_E}{C_c}
\frac{3}{32}(\theta_0\kappa)^2
\frac{\lambda_c}{\Lambda_E}.
\]

Hence, inside the already surviving transverse-support sector \(\Lambda_E\neq 0\),

\[
\operatorname{sgn}R_{\mathrm{exact}}
=
\operatorname{sgn}\!\Bigl(
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\frac{C_E}{C_c}\frac{\lambda_c}{\Lambda_E}
\Bigr).
\]

So the defect-sign information drops out:
only the relative sign of the longitudinal and transverse source packages matters.

The exact lowest-channel burden window is
\[
-1<R_{\mathrm{exact}}<1
\iff
\left|
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\frac{C_E}{C_c}
\frac{3}{32}(\theta_0\kappa)^2
\frac{\lambda_c}{\Lambda_E}
\right|<1.
\]

Equivalently,
\[
\left|\frac{\lambda_c}{\Lambda_E}\right|
<
\frac{32}{3}
\left|\frac{\xi_E}{\xi_c}\right|
\frac{C_c}{C_E}
\frac{1}{(\theta_0\kappa)^2}.
\]

At the working-branch leading level,
\[
\lambda_c^{(JJ)}
\sim
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\mathcal N_{JJ}m_\parallel u_\parallel |G_*|A_{G_*},
\qquad
\Lambda_E
=
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\mathfrak T_E,
\]
so
\[
R_{\mathrm{exact}}
\sim
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\frac{C_E}{C_c}
\frac{3}{32}(\theta_0\kappa)^2
\frac{\alpha_X}{\beta_X}
\frac{\mathcal N_{JJ}m_\parallel u_\parallel |G_*|A_{G_*}}{\mathfrak T_E}.
\]

Thus the third Gate-5 slot is fully reduced to a finite sign/size audit.

After this, only the remote-gap support scalar remains:
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{gap}}
=
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}-\eta_{R,\rho}.
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Exact Pass/Certificate Table for \texorpdfstring{$\Delta_{\mathrm{gap}}$}{Delta_gap}}

\section{Goal}

We now close the last remaining scalar in the current one-defect acceptance line:
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{gap}}
:=
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}-\eta_{R,\rho}.
\]

The purpose is not to restate the support theorem, but to convert it into a finite pass/certificate table for the intended explicit branch.

\section{1. Exact support theorem form}

The remote-gap support theorem has the fixed form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}>\eta_{R,\rho}
\Longrightarrow
\Delta_\rho
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}-\eta_{R,\rho}>0.
}
\label{eq:G1_support_master}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{gap}}>0
\Longrightarrow
\Delta_\rho>0.
}
\label{eq:G1_gap_scalar}
\end{equation}

Thus the final scalar in the present line is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{gap}}
=
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}-\eta_{R,\rho}.
}
\label{eq:Dgap_def_again}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Sectorwise benchmark decomposition}

The working finite benchmark is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
\Biggr\}.
}
\label{eq:G1_bench_master}
\end{equation}

Define the four benchmark slots
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B_{\mathrm{high}}:=4K-|r_*|,
\qquad
B_{\mathrm{vol}}:=\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
}
\label{eq:G1_B12}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B_{\mathrm{int}}
:=
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2q_*^2}
\right|,
\qquad
B_{\mathrm{non}}
:=
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}.
}
\label{eq:G1_B34}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
=
\min\{B_{\mathrm{high}},B_{\mathrm{vol}},B_{\mathrm{int}},B_{\mathrm{non}}\}.
}
\label{eq:G1_bench_min}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Residual budget decomposition}

The residual side satisfies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta_{R,\rho}
\le
\eta_{R,\rho}^{\mathrm{tr}}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:G1_residual_split}
\end{equation}

Hence any explicit upper budget
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E_{\mathrm{rem}}
\ge
\eta_{R,\rho}
}
\label{eq:G1_Erem_def}
\end{equation}
yields the sufficient implication
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\min\{B_{\mathrm{high}},B_{\mathrm{vol}},B_{\mathrm{int}},B_{\mathrm{non}}\}>E_{\mathrm{rem}}
\Longrightarrow
\Delta_{\mathrm{gap}}>0.
}
\label{eq:G1_certificate_generic}
\end{equation}

This is the correct certificate form because \(E_{\mathrm{rem}}\) is an upper bound, not the exact remote norm in general.

\section{4. Canonical pure-even explicit branch}

For the explicit canonical pure-even branch, the benchmark and residual sides have already been assembled into one fully explicit sufficient inequality:
\begin{align}
\boxed{
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
\Xi_{\mathrm{non}}^{(1)}(\rho)
\Biggr\}
}
\nonumber\\
\boxed{
>
2\left[
\kappa\rho(|C_E|+|C_O|)
+
\frac{1}{M_X^2}\left(\alpha_X^2+|\alpha_X\beta_X|+\beta_X^2\right)
\right]
+
2C_{\mathrm{high,non}}\rho
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}}K_a\rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}}\frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:G1_explicit_full_again}
\end{align}

Here the same-shell benchmark slot is explicitly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Xi_{\mathrm{non}}^{(1)}(\rho)
:=
\left|
-\mu^2+\frac{Zq_*^2}{4}-\frac{Yq_*^4}{16}+12uA^2
\right|
-
4uA^2
-
2a_K\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:G1_Xinon_again}
\end{equation}

If the pure-even branch is also enforced on the residual transport side, one may sharpen
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|C_E|+|C_O|
\;\longrightarrow\;
|C_E|.
}
\label{eq:G1_pureeven_sharpen}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Exact pass/certificate table}

We now rewrite \eqref{eq:G1_explicit_full_again} into a direct decision table.

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E_{\mathrm{rem}}^{\mathrm{(even)}}
:=
2\left[
\kappa\rho(|C_E|+|C_O|)
+
\frac{1}{M_X^2}\left(\alpha_X^2+|\alpha_X\beta_X|+\beta_X^2\right)
\right]
+
2C_{\mathrm{high,non}}\rho
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}}K_a\rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}}\frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:G1_Erem_even}
\end{equation}

Then the explicit branch certificate is

>
E_{\mathrm{rem}}^{\mathrm{(even)}}.

\end{equation}

Since

\min\{x_1,x_2,x_3,x_4\}>y
\iff
x_i>y\ \text{for all }i,
\]
\eqref{eq:G1_explicit_certificate} is equivalent to the four simultaneous inequalities
\begin{equation}

B_{\mathrm{high}}>E_{\mathrm{rem}}^{\mathrm{(even)}},

\end{equation}
\begin{equation}

B_{\mathrm{int}}>E_{\mathrm{rem}}^{\mathrm{(even)}},

\label{eq:G1_slot_non}
\end{equation}

Therefore the exact explicit pass table is:

Importantly, this is \emph{not} yet a proof of actual Gate-1 failure, because

or
\item an alternative spectral obstruction, e.g. a negative/nonpositive Gershgorin lower bound at the actual remote block level.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Actual Residual-Symmetry Closure of Gate 4}

\section{Goal}

We now push Gate 4 to its actual endpoint inside the current line.

The theorem-level reduction was already known:
\[
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\}

is the exact mass-protection criterion, and exact residual valley \(U(1)_V\) or already exact \(\mathbb Z_2^V\) is sufficient.

The only remaining question is whether the \emph{actual corrected microscopic branch} preserves the same residual generator through all constant corrections and remote elimination.

\section{1. Actual projected shell block and its residual generator}

For the actual projected massless shell block, the principal-symbol core has the form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)
=
v_\parallel p_\parallel\,\tau_3\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
\nu_1 p_1\,\tau_1\otimes s_1
+
\nu_2 p_2\,\tau_1\otimes s_2.
}
\label{eq:G4_actual_core}
\end{equation}

Its commutant is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{Comm}(\Gamma_1,\Gamma_2,\Gamma_3)
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}\{\mathbf 1_4,\ Q_*\},
\qquad
Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3.
}
\label{eq:G4_actual_commutant}
\end{equation}

Therefore the actual projected shell block carries an exact continuous residual symmetry
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U(1)_V^{\mathrm{(actual)}}:\qquad
U_\theta=e^{i\theta Q_*/2}.
}
\label{eq:G4_actual_U1}
\end{equation}

The weaker remnant
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathbb Z_2^V:\qquad
S_V:=Q_*,
\qquad
S_V^2=\mathbf 1_4,
}
\label{eq:G4_actual_Z2}
\end{equation}
is automatically present as a subgroup.

\section{2. Actual constant mass space}

The actual constant Dirac-mass space of this projected block is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}\{M_1,M_2\},
\qquad
M_1=\tau_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\quad
M_2=\tau_1\otimes s_3.
}
\label{eq:G4_actual_massspace}
\end{equation}

Under the exact residual \(U(1)_V^{\mathrm{(actual)}}\), these rotate as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_\theta M_1 U_\theta^{-1}
=
\cos\theta\,M_1+\sin\theta\,M_2,
}
\label{eq:G4_actual_rot1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_\theta M_2 U_\theta^{-1}
=
-\sin\theta\,M_1+\cos\theta\,M_2.
}
\label{eq:G4_actual_rot2}
\end{equation}

Hence no nonzero element of \(\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}\) is invariant under the full \(U(1)\):
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{U(1)_V^{\mathrm{(actual)}}}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:G4_actual_U1_forbid}
\end{equation}

Even the weaker discrete remnant already suffices, since
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_V M_1 S_V^{-1}=-M_1,
\qquad
S_V M_2 S_V^{-1}=-M_2,
}
\label{eq:G4_actual_Z2_odd}
\end{equation}
so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{\mathbb Z_2^V}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:G4_actual_Z2_forbid}
\end{equation}

Therefore the actual projected shell block is already mass-protected at the principal-symbol level.

What remains is only whether the \emph{full corrected microscopic block}, including all constant corrections and remote-sector elimination, preserves the same \(Q_*\).

This is the precise meaning of the residual-symmetry audit.

Let the final corrected constant block be written schematically as

The practical full-basis Gate-4 theorem states that if the same \(Q_*\) commutes with all three pieces, namely

\[
[Q_*,H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0,
\qquad
[Q_*,\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0,
\qquad

\section{5. Why this is enough}

If \eqref{eq:G4_comm1}--\eqref{eq:G4_comm3} hold, then the full corrected constant block is invariant under the same exact residual \(U(1)_V^{\mathrm{(actual)}}\) generated by \(Q_*\).
Therefore every residual-symmetry-allowed constant operator belongs to the \(Q_*\)-commutant.

But the actual mass space \(\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}\) transforms nontrivially under this \(U(1)\), equivalently is odd under the \(\mathbb Z_2\) remnant.
Hence no nonzero element of \(\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}\) can belong to the residual allowed algebra, and
\[
A_{\mathrm{res}}^{(\mathrm{full})}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.

Thus Gate 4 passes.

\begin{proof}

A_{\mathrm{res}}^{(\mathrm{full})}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.

M_2=\tau_1\otimes s_3.
\]

Under this exact residual \(U(1)\), the two mass generators rotate as a charged doublet, so
\[
A_{U(1)_V^{\mathrm{(actual)}}}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
\]
Already the weaker remnant \(\mathbb Z_2^V\) suffices.

Therefore the actual projected shell block itself is mass-protected at the principal-symbol level.

The only remaining microscopic question is whether the same \(Q_*\) survives all constant corrections and remote elimination.

If
\[
[Q_*,H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0,
\qquad
[Q_*,\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0,
\qquad
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0,
\]
then
\[
A_{\mathrm{res}}^{(\mathrm{full})}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\},
\]
and Gate 4 passes.

So Gate 4 is no longer a symmetry-discovery problem.
It is a finite verification problem for the preservation of an already identified residual generator.
