\section{Closure of the Remote Schur Part of Gate 4 via the \texorpdfstring{$Q_R$}{QR}-Intertwiner Route}

\section{Goal}

Inside the current branch, Gate 4 has already been reduced to the triple commutator test
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0,
\qquad
[Q_*,\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0,
\qquad
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
}
\label{eq:G4_goal_triple}
\end{equation}

For the present refined locked \(+\) Class II branch, the second commutator is already closed,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0,
}
\label{eq:G4_ClassII_closed}
\end{equation}
and after removal of the dangerous scalar identity-channel obstruction, the allowed low-block constant sector is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{const}}=a_0\mathbf 1_4+a_*Q_*,
}
\label{eq:G4_lowblock_form}
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0.
}
\label{eq:G4_lowblock_comm}
\end{equation}

Therefore the only remaining microscopic Gate-4 frontier is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
}
\label{eq:G4_only_remaining}
\end{equation}

\section{1. Actual canonical basis data}

In the actual canonical shell basis,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3,
}
\label{eq:G4_Qstar_actual}
\end{equation}
and the actual constant mass space is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}\{M_1,M_2\},
\qquad
M_1=\tau_2\otimes\mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
M_2=\tau_1\otimes s_3.
}
\label{eq:G4_Mactual_again}
\end{equation}

Let
\[
\mathcal C_{Q_*}
=
\{K\in\mathrm{Herm}(4):[Q_*,K]=0\}
\]
be the Hermitian \(Q_*\)-commutant. Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal C_{Q_*}\cap\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:G4_commutant_intersection}
\end{equation}

Therefore every exact constant operator commuting with \(Q_*\) is automatically mass-protecting.

\section{2. Block form of the full Hamiltonian}

Write the full zero-momentum block Hamiltonian as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{full}}(0)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_L(0) & V(0)\\
V(0)^\dagger & H_R(0)
\end{pmatrix},
}
\label{eq:G4_block_full}
\end{equation}
where:
\begin{itemize}
\item \(H_L(0)\) is the isolated low shell carrier block,
\item \(H_R(0)\) is the remote block,
\item \(V(0)\) is the constant low--remote mixing block.
\end{itemize}

The remote Schur self-energy is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Sigma(0,0)=V(0)\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}V(0)^\dagger.
}
\label{eq:G4_sigma_def}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Exact residual intertwiner route}

A sufficient executable Route II is the existence of a Hermitian generator \(Q_R\) on the remote sector such that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*\oplus Q_R,H_{\mathrm{full}}(0)]=0.
}
\label{eq:G4_routeII_master}
\end{equation}

Blockwise this is equivalent to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,H_L(0)]=0,
\qquad
[Q_R,H_R(0)]=0,
\qquad
Q_*V(0)=V(0)Q_R.
}
\label{eq:G4_routeII_blockwise}
\end{equation}

The practical statement in the actual-basis attachment is identical:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,H_L]=0,
\qquad
[Q_R,H_R]=0,
\qquad
Q_*W=WQ_R
\Longrightarrow
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
}
\label{eq:G4_routeII_attachment}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Direct proof that \texorpdfstring{$[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0$}{[Q*,Sigma]=0}}

Since \([Q_R,H_R(0)]=0\), the remote resolvent also commutes with \(Q_R\):
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_R\,H_R(0)^{-1}=H_R(0)^{-1}Q_R.
}
\label{eq:G4_resolvent_comm}
\end{equation}

Now compute:
\begin{align}
Q_*\,\Sigma(0,0)
&=
Q_*V(0)\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}V(0)^\dagger
\nonumber\\
&=
V(0)Q_R\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}V(0)^\dagger
\nonumber\\
&=
V(0)\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}Q_RV(0)^\dagger
\nonumber\\
&=
V(0)\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}V(0)^\dagger Q_*
\nonumber\\
&=
\Sigma(0,0)\,Q_*.
\end{align}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
}
\label{eq:G4_sigma_comm_exact}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Sigma(0,0)\in\mathcal C_{Q_*}.
}
\label{eq:G4_sigma_in_commutant}
\end{equation}

Using \eqref{eq:G4_commutant_intersection}, this implies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Sigma(0,0)\cap\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:G4_sigma_nomass}
\end{equation}

So the remote Schur part cannot generate an exact constant Dirac mass.

\section{5. Charge-sector formulation}

The most practical implementation of Route II is to decompose the remote sector into \(Q_R\)-charge sectors:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_R=\bigoplus_{q\in\mathcal Q}\mathcal H_R^{(q)},
\qquad
Q_R|_{\mathcal H_R^{(q)}}=q\,\mathbf 1.
}
\label{eq:G4_charge_remote}
\end{equation}

Similarly the low shell carrier decomposes under \(Q_*\) into
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_D=\mathcal H_D^{(+)}\oplus\mathcal H_D^{(-)}.
}
\label{eq:G4_charge_low}
\end{equation}

Then the intertwiner condition
\[
Q_*V(0)=V(0)Q_R
\]
is equivalent to the charge-preserving selection rule
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V(0):\mathcal H_R^{(q)}\longrightarrow \mathcal H_D^{(q)}
\quad\text{only.}
}
\label{eq:G4_charge_selection}
\end{equation}

Thus the remote part of Gate 4 is reduced to the finite audit:
\begin{enumerate}
\item decompose \(\mathcal H_R\) into exact \(Q_R\)-charge sectors;
\item verify \([Q_R,H_R(0)]=0\);
\item verify that every nonzero block of \(V(0)\) preserves the charge;
\item conclude \([Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0\).
\end{enumerate}

\section{6. Final Gate-4 closure for the current branch}

For the current refined locked \(+\) Class II branch:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0,
\qquad
[Q_*,\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0
}
\label{eq:G4_two_closed}
\end{equation}
are already the natural working conclusions.

If, in addition, there exists a Hermitian \(Q_R\) satisfying
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_R,H_R]=0,
\qquad
Q_*W=WQ_R,
}
\label{eq:G4_QR_final_cond}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
}
\label{eq:G4_QR_final_sigma}
\end{equation}

Therefore the full corrected constant sector
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta H_{\mathrm{const}}
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{const}}
+
\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}^{\mathrm{const}}
+
\Sigma(0,0)
}
\label{eq:G4_dHconst_final}
\end{equation}
belongs to the \(Q_*\)-commutant,
\[
\delta H_{\mathrm{const}}\in\mathcal C_{Q_*},
\]
and thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{\mathrm{res}}^{(\mathrm{full})}\cap\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:G4_final_pass}
\end{equation}

So Gate 4 passes.

\section{7. Honest remaining frontier}

At this point Gate 4 is no longer conceptually open.

The remaining microscopic work is only one of the following finite audits:
\begin{enumerate}
\item Route I: prove strict remote mismatch
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0,
\]
or
\item Route II: explicitly construct \(Q_R\) and verify
\[
[Q_R,H_R]=0,\qquad Q_*W=WQ_R.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Therefore the current branch has reduced Gate 4 completely to a finite symmetry/intertwiner verification problem.

\section{Final Summary}

The actual canonical basis already provides
\[
Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3,
\qquad

=

with

Hence every exact constant operator commuting with \(Q_*\) is automatically mass-protecting. :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}

So the remaining Gate-4 work is no longer conceptual.

\section{Route-II Charge-Table Audit and the Actual Closure of Gate 4}

\qquad

So, for the current branch,

Route II is the constructive route needed only if the truncation is enlarged and a dangerous extra remote sector appears:

Then the remaining Gate-4 task is the finite audit
\[
\exists\,Q_R:\ [Q_R,H_R(0)]=0,
\qquad

\section{3. Low-shell charge decomposition}

So the low block is already split into \(Q_*\)-charges \(+1\) and \(-1\).

\section{4. Remote-sector charge decomposition}

For an enlarged dangerous truncation, decompose the remote sector as
\[

=

\oplus

\oplus

}

Define the remote charge operator by
\[
\boxed{
Q_R|_{\mathcal H_R^{(+)}}=+1,
\qquad
Q_R|_{\mathcal H_R^{(-)}}=-1,
\qquad
Q_R|_{\mathcal H_R^{(0)}}=0.
}
\]

Equivalently, in projector language,

\[
\boxed{

where \(Q_0\) is any Hermitian involution on the neutral sector satisfying
\[
Q_0^2=R_0,
\qquad
[Q_0,H_R^{(0)}]=0.
\]

Then \(Q_R\) is Hermitian and
\[
[Q_R,H_R(0)]=0
\]
once the remote block is charge-block-diagonal.

\section{5. Charge-preserving coupling assumption}

The exact Route-II intertwiner condition is
\[
Q_*V(0)=V(0)Q_R.

In block form this is equivalent to the charge-selection rule
\[
\boxed{
V(0):\mathcal H_R^{(q)}\longrightarrow \mathcal H_D^{(q)}
\quad\text{only.}
}

Equivalently,

V(0)=P_+V(0)R_+ + P_-V(0)R_-,

with
\[
P_+V(0)R_-=0,
\qquad
P_-V(0)R_+=0,
\qquad
V(0)R_0=0.
\]

So the finite Route-II audit is exactly:

\begin{enumerate}
\item decompose \(\mathcal H_R\) into \(Q_R\)-charge sectors;
\item verify \(H_R(0)\) is block diagonal in \(q=+1,-1,0\), equivalently \([Q_R,H_R(0)]=0\);
\item verify every nonzero low--remote coupling block preserves charge:
\[
V(0):\mathcal H_R^{(q)}\to\mathcal H_D^{(q)}\quad\text{only.}
\]
\end{enumerate}

\section{6. Schur self-energy inheritance}

Under

[Q_R,H_R(0)]=0,

the remote resolvent commutes with \(Q_R\), and therefore

So the remote self-energy cannot generate a constant actual Dirac mass.

\section{Final Summary}

For the remote-sector part of Gate 4 there are two exact routes.

\text{the only remaining carrier question is the survival of the primitive longitudinal channel.}
}
\label{eq:explicit_branch_remaining_only}
\end{equation}

So the explicit branch admissibility problem has been reduced to:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{

\qquad
\text{Gate 4: closed in the working truncation,}
\qquad
\text{Gate 2: final unresolved microscopic audit.}
}
\label{eq:explicit_branch_status_triplet}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The carrier-level acceptance logic is

\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad

At the current stage:

\section{Actual Pass Stamp of the Calibration Layer}

\section{1. Exact calibration layer}

The exact reduced coefficient extraction is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3M^\parallel),
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=\frac14\Tr(\sigma_1M_1+\sigma_2M_2),
\qquad
\beta=\frac14\Tr(\sigma_2M_1-\sigma_1M_2).
}
\end{equation}

The exact Bloch/transport normalization layer is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=C_\parallel g_c,
\qquad
\alpha=C_E g_E,
\qquad
\beta=C_O g_O.
}
\label{eq:exact_norm_layer}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c=\frac{\lambda_\parallel}{C_\parallel},
\qquad
g_E=\frac{\alpha}{C_E},
\qquad
g_O=\frac{\beta}{C_O}.
}
\label{eq:exact_norm_layer_inverse}
\end{equation}

Thus the calibration constants are not new dynamical coefficients.
They are the overlap-normalization factors converting the reduced shell coefficients
\[
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)
\]
into the transport-normalized one-defect data
\[
(g_c,g_E,g_O).
\]

\section{2. Concrete one-mediator explicit branch}

In the concrete one-mediator truncation, the microscopic effective cross terms are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{eff}}
\supset
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}J_i^aK_i^a
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}K_i^a\mathcal E_i^a
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}K_i^a\mathcal O_i^a.
}
\end{equation}

The corresponding normalized overlap constants are defined by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_\parallel:=A_a(\theta)k_a(\theta)\big|_{\mathrm{normalized}},
}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_E:=\text{normalized coefficient of }K_i^a\mathcal E_i^a,
\qquad
C_O:=\text{normalized coefficient of }K_i^a\mathcal O_i^a.
}
\end{equation}

Hence the explicit concrete coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c^{(1)}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,C_\parallel,
}
\label{eq:lambda_c_concrete}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_E^{(1)}
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}\,C_E,
\qquad
\widetilde\Lambda_O^{(1)}
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,C_O.
}
\label{eq:Lambda_EO_concrete}
\end{equation}

Therefore the concrete witness branch already shows that the entire calibration layer is absorbed into the three overlap factors
\[
C_\parallel,\qquad C_E,\qquad C_O.
\]

\section{3. Canonical explicit normalization}

The crucial practical simplification is that in the canonical explicit normalization one may choose
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_\parallel=C_E=C_O=1.
}
\label{eq:canonical_overlap_norm}
\end{equation}

With this choice,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c^{(1)}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2},
\qquad
\widetilde\Lambda_E^{(1)}
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2},
\qquad
\widetilde\Lambda_O^{(1)}
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}.
}
\label{eq:canonical_mediator_coeffs}
\end{equation}

At the shell-block level, the explicit canonical Branch-B block becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M^\parallel
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{2M_X^2}I_3\,\sigma_3,
}
\label{eq:Mpar_canonical}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M^1
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}J_1\,\sigma_1
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}J_1\,\sigma_2,
}
\label{eq:M1_canonical}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M^2
=
+\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}J_1\,\sigma_1
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}J_1\,\sigma_2.
}
\label{eq:M2_canonical}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{2M_X^2}I_3\,p_\parallel\sigma_3
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}J_1\,(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}J_1\,(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
}
\label{eq:A1_canonical_branchB}
\end{equation}

So on the explicit canonical witness branch, the calibration layer does not suppress any nonzero transport coefficient:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_\parallel=C_E=C_O=1
\Longrightarrow
g_c=\lambda_\parallel,\qquad
g_E=\alpha,\qquad
g_O=\beta.
}
\label{eq:no_calibration_obstruction}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Practical carrier pass stamp after calibration}

Recall the current carrier-side status:

\begin{enumerate}
\item Gate 4 is already closed in the working truncation;
\item Gate 3 is effectively passed once the explicit branch realizes a nonzero transverse witness and \((C_E,C_O)\neq(0,0)\);
\item Gate 2 is reduced to the practical witness condition
\[
|\Delta_{00}\alpha_XL_*A_{G_*}|>|R_N|
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Under the canonical explicit normalization \eqref{eq:canonical_overlap_norm}, the calibration conditions become automatic:
\[
C_\parallel\neq 0,\qquad (C_E,C_O)\neq (0,0).
\]

Therefore the carrier-level practical pass stamp reduces to the transport-side witness conditions alone.

\begin{theorem}[Practical carrier pass stamp on the explicit canonical witness branch]
Assume:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the working truncation is the current refined locked \(+\) Class II branch;
\item the shell tangent basis is canonically normalized so that
\[
C_\parallel=C_E=C_O=1;
\]
\item Gate 4 is closed in the working truncation;
\item the explicit transverse branch realizes a nonzero witness pair
\[
(c_E,c_O)\neq(0,0);
\]
\item the longitudinal Branch-B witness satisfies
\[
|\Delta_{00}\alpha_XL_*A_{G_*}|>|R_N|.
\]
\end{enumerate}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq(0,0),
}
\end{equation}
hence the branch passes the carrier-level practical admissibility test.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Under canonical normalization,
\[
C_\parallel=C_E=C_O=1,
\]
so the exact normalization layer becomes
\[
g_c=\lambda_\parallel,\qquad
g_E=\alpha,\qquad
g_O=\beta.
\]
Therefore no nonzero transport witness is killed by the Bloch overlap layer.

The longitudinal witness implies \(\lambda_\parallel\neq 0\).
The transverse witness implies \((\alpha,\beta)\neq(0,0)\).
Together with the already closed Gate 4, this is exactly the carrier-level admissibility condition.
\end{proof}

\section{5. Honest scope of this closure}

This does \emph{not} mean that the final complete microscopic TECT action has already been fully and unconditionally calibrated.

What it means is narrower and honest:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{on the strongest explicit canonical witness branch,}
\quad
\text{the normalization layer itself is no longer an obstruction.}
}
\end{equation}

The remaining frontier of the full theory is still the actual coefficient extraction from the final complete TECT operator,
\[
L(k)\to K_i\to P_*K_iP_*\to (\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta),
\]
not the algebraic form of the calibration layer.

\section{Final Summary}

The exact calibration layer is
\[
\lambda_\parallel=C_\parallel g_c,
\qquad
\alpha=C_E g_E,
\qquad
\beta=C_O g_O,
\]
equivalently
\[
g_c=\frac{\lambda_\parallel}{C_\parallel},
\qquad
g_E=\frac{\alpha}{C_E},
\qquad
g_O=\frac{\beta}{C_O}.
\]

In the concrete one-mediator explicit branch, the calibration constants are the normalized overlap factors appearing in
\[
\lambda_c^{(1)}=-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}C_\parallel,
\qquad
\widetilde\Lambda_E^{(1)}=-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}C_E,
\qquad
\widetilde\Lambda_O^{(1)}=-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}C_O.
\]

In the canonical explicit normalization one may choose
\[
\boxed{
C_\parallel=C_E=C_O=1.
}
\]

Therefore, on the explicit canonical witness branch,
\[
\boxed{
g_c=\lambda_\parallel,
\qquad
g_E=\alpha,
\qquad
g_O=\beta.
}
\]

So the calibration layer no longer kills any nonzero transport witness.

Hence the practical carrier pass stamp becomes:

if
\[
|\Delta_{00}\alpha_XL_*A_{G_*}|>|R_N|,
\qquad
(c_E,c_O)\neq(0,0),
\]
and Gate 4 is already closed in the working truncation, then
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq(0,0),
}
\]
so the explicit canonical witness branch passes the carrier-level practical admissibility test.

This is an honest working-branch closure.
It does not yet replace the final complete microscopic coefficient extraction from the full TECT operator.

\section{Orthodox Completion Route from the Microscopic TECT Defect Operator}

\section{1. Honest endpoint of the previous line}

The previous witness/certificate line should now be regarded as complete at its honest endpoint.

What it achieved is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{support theorems, carrier witness structure, and one-defect finite audit are in place.}
}
\end{equation}

What it did \emph{not} yet achieve is the true first-principles microscopic derivation.
The genuinely unfinished core remains:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{derive the actual TECT defect fluctuation operator and compute the explicit microscopic overlap coefficients.}
}
\end{equation}

Therefore the correct next step is no longer another auxiliary theorem.
It is to return to the main line:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{microscopic TECT defect PDE}
\;\longrightarrow\;
\text{single-defect operator}
\;\longrightarrow\;
\text{single-defect zero mode}
\;\longrightarrow\;
\text{three-defect projector}
\;\longrightarrow\;
\text{sectoral overlap operator}.
}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Minimal microscopic multiplet and working action}

We adopt the minimal working microscopic multiplet
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak B=(P^A,\Psi,X_i^a).
}
\end{equation}

Here:
\begin{itemize}
\item \(P^A(x)\) is the locked condensate/order-parameter background,
\item \(\Psi(x)\) is the fluctuation field whose low spectral sector will generate the family space,
\item \(X_i^a(x)\) is the heavy Class-II mediator field.
\end{itemize}

The minimal structurally correct microscopic working ansatz is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal L_{\rm mic}
=
\mathcal L_\Psi^{\rm ref}[P,\Psi]
+
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha_X X_i^a J_i^a[P,\Psi]
+
\beta_X X_i^a K_i^a[P,\Psi].
}
\label{eq:mic_ansatz}
\end{equation}

The reference \(\Psi\)-sector is taken in first-order form:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal L_\Psi^{\rm ref}
=
\Psi^\dagger
\Bigl(
iK^0(P)\partial_t
+
iK^i(P)\partial_i
-
\mathcal M(P)
\Bigr)\Psi
+\cdots
}
\label{eq:psi_ref}
\end{equation}
where \(K^0(P)\), \(K^i(P)\), and \(\mathcal M(P)\) are constitutive TECT coefficient fields.

\section{3. Defect background and linearization}

Choose a static one-defect background
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\bar P(x),\qquad \bar X_i^a(x),
}
\end{equation}
with asymptotic bulk limit
\[
\bar P(x)\to P_\infty,\qquad \bar X_i^a(x)\to X_{i,\infty}^a
\qquad (|x|\to\infty).
\]

Now linearize the microscopic equations around the defect:
\[
P=\bar P+\pi,\qquad
X=\bar X+\chi,\qquad
\Psi=\bar\Psi+\psi.
\]
Keeping only the fluctuation operator acting on \(\psi\), one obtains
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
iG_{\rm def}^0(x)\,\partial_t\psi
=
\Bigl(
-iG_{\rm def}^i(x)\partial_i
+
M_{\rm def}(x)
\Bigr)\psi
+
W_{\rm def}(x)\chi
+\cdots
}
\label{eq:lin_defect_eq}
\end{equation}
with defect-background coefficients
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
G_{\rm def}^0=K^0(\bar P,\bar X),
\qquad
G_{\rm def}^i=K^i(\bar P,\bar X),
\qquad
M_{\rm def}=\mathcal M(\bar P,\bar X,\partial\bar P,\partial\bar X).
}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Elimination of the heavy mediator}

At leading order in the heavy-mediator approximation, the \(\chi\)-equation is algebraic:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_X^2\,\chi_i^a
+
\alpha_X\,\delta J_i^a
+
\beta_X\,\delta K_i^a
=0
+O(\partial\chi,\chi^2).
}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\chi_i^a
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\bigl(
\alpha_X\,\delta J_i^a
+
\beta_X\,\delta K_i^a
\bigr)
+O(M_X^{-4}).
}
\label{eq:heavy_X_sol}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:heavy_X_sol} back into \eqref{eq:lin_defect_eq} gives a closed effective linear fluctuation equation for \(\psi\):
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
i\widehat G_{\rm def}^0(x)\,\partial_t\psi
=
\Bigl(
-i\widehat G_{\rm def}^i(x)\partial_i
+
\widehat M_{\rm def}(x)
\Bigr)\psi
}
\label{eq:closed_lin_eq}
\end{equation}
where the hatted coefficients include the Class-II Schur-complement correction.

This is the first genuinely orthodox microscopic step:
the effective single-defect operator is now derived from the microscopic defect background rather than postulated as an abstract matrix ansatz.

\section{5. Canonical first-order defect operator}

Assume \(\widehat G_{\rm def}^0(x)\) is Hermitian and positive in the asymptotic bulk and remains invertible along the defect profile.
Then we canonically normalize the time-kinetic factor:
\[
\psi=(\widehat G_{\rm def}^0)^{-1/2}\,\widetilde\psi.
\]
The equation becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
i\partial_t\widetilde\psi
=
\mathbb O_{\rm 1def}^{(0)}\widetilde\psi,
}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathbb O_{\rm 1def}^{(0)}
=
i\widetilde\Gamma_{\rm def}^i(\partial_i+\Omega_i^{\rm def})
+\Phi_{\rm def},
}
\label{eq:orthodox_def_op}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde\Gamma_{\rm def}^i
=
(\widehat G_{\rm def}^0)^{-1/2}\widehat G_{\rm def}^i(\widehat G_{\rm def}^0)^{-1/2},
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Omega_i^{\rm def}
=
\frac12(\widehat G_{\rm def}^0)^{1/2}\partial_i(\widehat G_{\rm def}^0)^{-1/2}
+\Omega_{i,\rm mic}^{\rm def},
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Phi_{\rm def}
=
(\widehat G_{\rm def}^0)^{-1/2}\widehat M_{\rm def}(\widehat G_{\rm def}^0)^{-1/2}.
}
\end{equation}

Thus the abstract reference-operator template is now promoted to the actual microscopic target of the orthodox TECT program.

\section{6. The single-defect zero-mode problem}

The single-defect light-mode equation is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathbb O_{\rm 1def}^{(0)}\psi_\star=0.
}
\label{eq:zero_mode_eq}
\end{equation}

The theorem schema to be completed inside TECT is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Fredholm / Callias structure}
+
\text{asymptotic bulk invertibility}
+
\text{grading}
+
\operatorname{Ind}\bigl(\mathbb O_{\rm 1def}^{(0)}\bigr)=1
\Longrightarrow
\dim\ker \mathbb O_{\rm 1def}^{(0)}=1
\text{ in the protected light sector.}
}
\label{eq:callias_schema}
\end{equation}

At present this is still conditional in TECT.
So the honest next mathematical tasks are:
\begin{enumerate}
\item prove self-adjointness / Fredholmness of \(\mathbb O_{\rm 1def}^{(0)}\),
\item prove asymptotic invertibility of \(\Phi_{\rm def}\),
\item identify the relevant topological class,
\item prove
\[
\operatorname{Ind}(\mathbb O_{\rm 1def}^{(0)})=1.
\]
\end{enumerate}

\section{7. Three-defect family projector}

If the single-defect theorem is established and the isolated defect centered at \(X_a\) supports a localized mode
\[
\psi_\star(x-X_a),
\qquad a=1,2,3,
\]
then for sufficiently separated defects the three-defect operator
\[
\mathbb O_{\rm 3def}^{(0)}
\]
has an isolated low-energy three-state cluster.

The exact family projector is then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
P_L
=
\frac{1}{2\pi i}\oint_\Gamma
(z-\mathbb O_{\rm 3def}^{(0)})^{-1}\,dz,
}
\label{eq:family_projector}
\end{equation}
with
\[
\operatorname{rank}P_L=3,
\qquad
\mathcal H_L=\operatorname{Ran}(P_L).
\]

This is the orthodox derivation of the family space:
it is not assumed, but extracted spectrally from the microscopic three-defect operator.

\section{8. Sectoral overlap operators}

For each sector \(f\in\{u,d,e,\nu\}\), the microscopic sectoral family operator is obtained by projection:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal Y_f
=
P_L\,\delta\mathbb O_f\,P_L
-
P_L\,\delta\mathbb O_f\,Q_H
(\mathbb O_H)^{-1}
Q_H\,\delta\mathbb O_f\,P_L
+\cdots,
}
\label{eq:sectoral_operator}
\end{equation}
where \(Q_H=1-P_L\) is the heavy-sector complement.

In a family basis \(\{\phi_1,\phi_2,\phi_3\}\subset \mathcal H_L\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(M_f)_{ab}
=
\langle \phi_a,\mathcal Y_f\phi_b\rangle.
}
\label{eq:family_matrix}
\end{equation}

This is the exact orthodox analogue of the overlap-integral construction in string/KK models:
the effective family operator is derived from the microscopic zero-mode wavefunctions and their projected couplings.

\section{9. Relation to the previous witness chain}

The previous reduced witness chain
\[
P_B
\to
V^\mu
\to
u^\pm
\to
(M^\mu)_{ab}
\to
P_*K_iP_*
\to
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)
\]
is now reinterpreted correctly:
it is not the final theory, but the shell-projected low-energy shadow of the orthodox microscopic chain
\[
\mathfrak B
\to
\mathbb O_{\rm 1def}^{(0)}
\to
\psi_\star
\to
P_L
\to
\mathcal Y_f.
\]

So the two are consistent, but the latter is the fundamental route.

\section{10. Final sharp status}

The operator-theoretic and coefficient-extraction skeleton is now fixed.
What remains open is not the route itself, but the actual TECT constitutive insertion:
\[
Z^0(P),\quad
Z^i(P),\quad
M_0(P),\quad
A_i^a(P),\quad
B_{ij}^a(P),\quad
C_i^a(P),\quad
D_{ij}^a(P),
\]
the explicit locked BCC defect background \((\bar P,\bar X)\),
the asymptotic bulk invertibility proof,
the grading/index analysis,
and the actual overlap integrals.

Hence the correct orthodox completion problem is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{insert the actual TECT constitutive data into the already-fixed microscopic operator skeleton.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The previous witness/certificate line should now be regarded as complete at its honest endpoint.

The correct orthodox route is:

\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak B=(P^A,\Psi,X_i^a)
\;\longrightarrow\;
\mathbb O_{\rm 1def}^{(0)}
\;\longrightarrow\;
\ker \mathbb O_{\rm 1def}^{(0)}
\;\longrightarrow\;
P_L
\;\longrightarrow\;
\mathcal Y_f.
}
\]

The minimal microscopic working action is
\[
\mathcal L_{\rm mic}
=
\mathcal L_\Psi^{\rm ref}[P,\Psi]
+
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha_X X_i^aJ_i^a[P,\Psi]
+
\beta_X X_i^aK_i^a[P,\Psi].
\]

Linearizing around a static defect background \((\bar P,\bar X)\) and eliminating the heavy mediator gives the closed effective defect fluctuation equation
\[
i\widehat G_{\rm def}^0\,\partial_t\psi
=
\bigl(
-i\widehat G_{\rm def}^i\partial_i+\widehat M_{\rm def}
\bigr)\psi.
\]

After canonical normalization, this becomes the first-order defect operator
\[
\boxed{
\mathbb O_{\rm 1def}^{(0)}
=
i\widetilde\Gamma_{\rm def}^i(\partial_i+\Omega_i^{\rm def})
+\Phi_{\rm def}.
}
\]

The single-defect theorem to be completed inside TECT is:
\[
\text{Fredholm / Callias structure}
+
\text{asymptotic bulk invertibility}
+
\text{grading}
+
\operatorname{Ind}(\mathbb O_{\rm 1def}^{(0)})=1
\Longrightarrow
\text{one protected light mode.}
\]

If this is established, then for three sufficiently separated defects the family projector is
\[
P_L
=
\frac{1}{2\pi i}\oint_\Gamma
(z-\mathbb O_{\rm 3def}^{(0)})^{-1}\,dz,
\qquad
\operatorname{rank}P_L=3,
\]
and the sectoral family operator is obtained by projection:
\[
\mathcal Y_f
=
P_L\,\delta\mathbb O_f\,P_L
-
P_L\,\delta\mathbb O_f\,Q_H
(\mathbb O_H)^{-1}
Q_H\,\delta\mathbb O_f\,P_L
+\cdots.
\]

So the genuine unfinished core is no longer the witness algebra.
It is the actual TECT constitutive insertion into this already-fixed microscopic operator skeleton.

\section{Orthodox Step 1 on the Same Working Branch: Actual Defect Operator and Radial Reduction}

\section{1. Reuse-only principle}

We do \emph{not} introduce a new microscopic branch.
We keep exactly the same strongest explicit working branch used before.

Hence we reuse, without rederiving, the already fixed microscopic coefficient template
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal L_{\rm mic}
=
\mathcal L_P[P]
+
\frac{i}{2}\Psi^\dagger Z^0(P)\!\stackrel{\leftrightarrow}{\partial_t}\!\Psi
+
\frac{i}{2}\Psi^\dagger\Bigl(Z^i(P)+X_j^aV_{ji}^a(P)\Bigr)\!\stackrel{\leftrightarrow}{\partial_i}\!\Psi
-
\Psi^\dagger\Bigl(M_0(P)-X_i^aU_i^a(P)\Bigr)\Psi
+
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a.
}
\label{eq:same_working_branch}
\end{equation}

We also reuse the same minimal constitutive ansatz
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Z^0(P)=z_0(\sigma)\,\mathbf 1,
\qquad
Z^i(P)=v_\perp(\sigma)\Gamma^i+v_c(\sigma)\hat n^i\Gamma_{\hat n},
\qquad
M_0(P)=m(\sigma)\Gamma^\sharp,
}
\label{eq:reuse_ref_coeffs}
\end{equation}
and the same Class II local-current coefficients
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_i^a(P)=u_X(\sigma)\,E_i{}^a\,\Gamma^\sharp,
}
\label{eq:reuse_U}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_{ij}^a(P)
=
E_i{}^a
\Bigl[
v_E^{(X)}(\sigma)\,\delta_{j\ell}
+
v_O^{(X)}(\sigma)\,\epsilon_{j\ell m}\hat n_m
+
v_c^{(X)}(\sigma)\,\hat n_j\hat n_\ell
\Bigr]\Gamma^\ell.
}
\label{eq:reuse_V}
\end{equation}

All of the above are already fixed by the previous working-branch construction.
The new calculation begins only now.

\section{2. Radial single-defect background}

Take a static radial one-defect background centered at the origin:
\[
r:=|x|,
\qquad
\hat n_i(x):=\frac{x_i}{r},
\qquad
\bar\sigma(x)=\bar\sigma(r).
\]

Choose the locked orthonormal frame \(E_i{}^a(x)\in SO(3)\) adapted to the defect,
\[
E_i{}^3(x)=\hat n_i(x),
\]
with \(E_i{}^1,E_i{}^2\) spanning the tangent frame on \(S^2\).

The most general rotationally covariant locked mediator profile is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\bar X_i{}^a(x)
=
X_\perp(r)\bigl(\delta_i{}^a-\hat n_i\hat n^a\bigr)
+
X_\parallel(r)\hat n_i\hat n^a.
}
\label{eq:radial_Xbar}
\end{equation}
Its locked scalar contraction is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\chi_X(r)
=
\frac13\,\bar X_i{}^aE_i{}^a
=
\frac13\bigl(2X_\perp(r)+X_\parallel(r)\bigr).
}
\label{eq:chiX_def}
\end{equation}

\section{3. New calculation: explicit defect coefficient fields}

Substituting the radial background \((\bar P,\bar X)\) into the reused constitutive template yields the actual microscopic defect coefficients.

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_E(r)
:=
v_\perp(\bar\sigma(r))
+
3\chi_X(r)\,v_E^{(X)}(\bar\sigma(r)),
}
\label{eq:gEeff}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_O(r)
:=
3\chi_X(r)\,v_O^{(X)}(\bar\sigma(r)),
}
\label{eq:gOeff}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c(r)
:=
v_c(\bar\sigma(r))
+
3\chi_X(r)\,v_c^{(X)}(\bar\sigma(r)),
}
\label{eq:gceff}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_{\rm eff}(r)
:=
m(\bar\sigma(r))
-
3\chi_X(r)\,u_X(\bar\sigma(r)).
}
\label{eq:meff}
\end{equation}

Then the actual defect coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K^0_{\rm def}(r)=z_0(\bar\sigma(r))\,\mathbf 1,
}
\label{eq:K0def}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K^i_{\rm def}(r)
=
g_E(r)\Gamma^i
+
g_O(r)\,\epsilon_{i\ell m}\hat n_m\Gamma^\ell
+
g_c(r)\hat n_i\Gamma_{\hat n}.
}
\label{eq:Kidef_raw}
\end{equation}

Introduce the transverse projector
\[
\Pi^\perp_{ij}:=\delta_{ij}-\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
\Gamma_i^\perp:=\Pi^\perp_{i\ell}\Gamma^\ell,
\qquad
\Gamma^i=\Gamma_i^\perp+\hat n_i\Gamma_{\hat n}.
\]
Also define
\[
J_i(\hat n):=\epsilon_{i\ell m}\hat n_m\Gamma^\ell.
\]
Since \(\hat n_iJ_i(\hat n)=0\), the transport tensor splits exactly into three channels:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K^i_{\rm def}(r)
=
g_E(r)\Gamma_i^\perp
+
g_R(r)\hat n_i\Gamma_{\hat n}
+
g_O(r)J_i(\hat n),
\qquad
g_R(r):=g_E(r)+g_c(r).
}
\label{eq:Kidef_split}
\end{equation}

This is the actual microscopic radial lift of the previously reduced \((g_E,g_O,g_c)\) channels.

\section{4. New calculation: explicit zeroth-order term}

We now compute the zeroth-order term
\[
M_{\rm def}
=
\frac{i}{2}\partial_iK^i_{\rm def}
-
m_{\rm eff}(r)\Gamma^\sharp.
\]

Using
\[
\partial_i\hat n_j=\frac1r\Pi^\perp_{ij},
\qquad
\partial_i\hat n_i=\frac2r,
\qquad
\partial_i\Gamma_{\hat n}
=
\frac1r\Pi^\perp_{ij}\Gamma^j,
\]
one finds:

\paragraph{Radial part.}
\[
\partial_i\bigl(g_R(r)\hat n_i\Gamma_{\hat n}\bigr)
=
\left(g_R'(r)+\frac{2g_R(r)}{r}\right)\Gamma_{\hat n}.
\]

\paragraph{Even tangential part.}
Since \(\hat n_i\Gamma_i^\perp=0\) and
\[
\partial_i\Gamma_i^\perp=-\frac{2}{r}\Gamma_{\hat n},
\]
one obtains
\[
\partial_i\bigl(g_E(r)\Gamma_i^\perp\bigr)
=
-\frac{2g_E(r)}{r}\Gamma_{\hat n}.
\]

\paragraph{Odd tangential part.}
Because
\[
\hat n_iJ_i(\hat n)=0,
\qquad
\partial_iJ_i(\hat n)=0,
\]
one gets
\[
\partial_i\bigl(g_O(r)J_i(\hat n)\bigr)=0.
\]

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_iK^i_{\rm def}(r)
=
\left(
g_R'(r)+\frac{2g_c(r)}{r}
\right)\Gamma_{\hat n}.
}
\label{eq:divK}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_{\rm def}(r)
=
\frac{i}{2}\left(
g_R'(r)+\frac{2g_c(r)}{r}
\right)\Gamma_{\hat n}
-
m_{\rm eff}(r)\Gamma^\sharp.
}
\label{eq:Mdef}
\end{equation}

This is a genuinely new step:
the actual defect zeroth-order operator is now explicit on the same working branch.

\section{5. Canonical normalization}

Let
\[
z(r):=z_0(\bar\sigma(r))>0.
\]
Since \(K^0_{\rm def}(r)=z(r)\mathbf 1\), the canonical normalization is scalar:
\[
S(r)=\sqrt{z(r)}\,\mathbf 1,
\qquad
\chi=S\psi.
\]

Then
\[
i\partial_t\chi=\mathbb H_{\rm def}\chi,
\]
with
\[
\mathbb H_{\rm def}
=
-i\,\Gamma_{\rm def}^i(r)\partial_i
+
W_{\rm def}(r,\hat n),
\]
and because \(S\) is scalar,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma_{\rm def}^i(r)=\frac{1}{z(r)}K_{\rm def}^i(r).
}
\label{eq:Gamdef}
\end{equation}

Define the normalized radial coefficients
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a(r):=\frac{g_R(r)}{z(r)},
\qquad
b(r):=\frac{g_E(r)}{z(r)},
\qquad
c(r):=\frac{g_O(r)}{z(r)},
\qquad
\mu(r):=\frac{m_{\rm eff}(r)}{z(r)}.
}
\label{eq:abcdmu}
\end{equation}

A direct computation gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W_{\rm def}(r,\hat n)
=
-i\,\omega_r(r)\Gamma_{\hat n}
+
\mu(r)\Gamma^\sharp,
}
\label{eq:Wdef}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\omega_r(r)
=
\frac{1}{2z(r)}
\left(
g_R'(r)+\frac{2g_c(r)}{r}-g_R(r)\frac{z'(r)}{z(r)}
\right).
}
\label{eq:omegar}
\end{equation}

Thus the canonically normalized defect operator is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathbb H_{\rm def}
=
-i\,a(r)\Gamma_{\hat n}\partial_r
-\frac{i\,b(r)}{r}\Gamma_i^\perp\nabla_i^{S^2}
-\frac{i\,c(r)}{r}J_i(\hat n)\nabla_i^{S^2}
-i\,\omega_r(r)\Gamma_{\hat n}
+\mu(r)\Gamma^\sharp.
}
\label{eq:Hdef_full}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Spherical Dirac reduction}

Define the spherical Dirac operator
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal D_{S^2}:=-i\,\Gamma_{\hat n}\Gamma_i^\perp\nabla_i^{S^2}.
}
\label{eq:Ds2}
\end{equation}
Using
\[
\Gamma_i^\perp\nabla_i^{S^2}=i\Gamma_{\hat n}\mathcal D_{S^2},
\qquad
J_i(\hat n)\nabla_i^{S^2}=-\mathcal D_{S^2},
\]
the operator becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathbb H_{\rm def}
=
-i\,a(r)\Gamma_{\hat n}\partial_r
+\frac{b(r)}{r}\Gamma_{\hat n}\mathcal D_{S^2}
+\frac{i\,c(r)}{r}\mathcal D_{S^2}
-i\,\omega_r(r)\Gamma_{\hat n}
+\mu(r)\Gamma^\sharp.
}
\label{eq:Hdef_compact}
\end{equation}

Now choose an angular eigenbasis \(Y_{\kappa m\varsigma}\) satisfying
\[
\mathcal D_{S^2}Y_{\kappa m\varsigma}=\kappa Y_{\kappa m\varsigma},
\qquad
\Gamma^\sharp Y_{\kappa m\varsigma}=\varsigma Y_{\kappa m\varsigma},
\qquad
\varsigma=\pm1.
\]
Because
\[
\{\Gamma_{\hat n},\mathcal D_{S^2}\}=0,
\qquad
\{\Gamma_{\hat n},\Gamma^\sharp\}=0,
\]
each channel closes on
\[
\operatorname{span}\{Y_{\kappa m\varsigma},\Gamma_{\hat n}Y_{\kappa m\varsigma}\}.
\]

Thus a stationary mode of energy \(\omega\) can be written as
\[
\chi(r,\Omega)=u(r)Y(\Omega)+v(r)\Gamma_{\hat n}Y(\Omega),
\]
and the full zero-mode problem reduces to the exact 1D first-order system
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\omega u
=
-i\,a(r)\,v'(r)
-i\,\omega_r(r)\,v(r)
-\frac{b(r)\kappa}{r}\,v(r)
+i\,\frac{c(r)\kappa}{r}\,u(r)
+\varsigma\,\mu(r)\,u(r),
}
\label{eq:radial1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\omega v
=
-i\,a(r)\,u'(r)
-i\,\omega_r(r)\,u(r)
+\frac{b(r)\kappa}{r}\,u(r)
-i\,\frac{c(r)\kappa}{r}\,v(r)
-\varsigma\,\mu(r)\,v(r).
}
\label{eq:radial2}
\end{equation}

This is the actual orthodox zero-mode equation on the same working branch.

\section{7. Gauge-removal of the radial connection term}

The \(\omega_r\)-term is kinematical and can be removed.
Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal I(r):=\exp\left(\int^r \frac{\omega_r(s)}{a(s)}\,ds\right),
}
\label{eq:Idef}
\end{equation}
and rescale
\[
u(r)=\mathcal I(r)^{-1}\widetilde u(r),
\qquad
v(r)=\mathcal I(r)^{-1}\widetilde v(r).
\]
Then the system becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\omega \widetilde u
=
-i\,a(r)\,\widetilde v'(r)
-\frac{b(r)\kappa}{r}\,\widetilde v(r)
+i\,\frac{c(r)\kappa}{r}\,\widetilde u(r)
+\varsigma\,\mu(r)\,\widetilde u(r),
}
\label{eq:redradial1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\omega \widetilde v
=
-i\,a(r)\,\widetilde u'(r)
+\frac{b(r)\kappa}{r}\,\widetilde u(r)
-i\,\frac{c(r)\kappa}{r}\,\widetilde v(r)
-\varsigma\,\mu(r)\,\widetilde v(r).
}
\label{eq:redradial2}
\end{equation}

So the genuinely dynamical coefficients are only
\[
a(r),\qquad b(r),\qquad c(r),\qquad \mu(r).
\]

\section{8. Precise relation to the previous working-branch audit}

The previous reduced witness/audit chain is recovered as the asymptotic or shell-projected shadow of these microscopic radial coefficients.

If the branch is asymptotically the simplest vacuum branch,
\[
X_{\perp,\infty}=X_{\parallel,\infty}=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\chi_{X,\infty}=0,
\]
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_E(\infty)=v_\perp(\sigma_\infty),
\qquad
g_O(\infty)=0,
\qquad
g_c(\infty)=v_c(\sigma_\infty),
\qquad
m_{\rm eff}(\infty)=m(\sigma_\infty).
}
\label{eq:asymmatch}
\end{equation}

Thus the old finite audit quantities are not discarded.
They are the asymptotic / projected reductions of the same actual microscopic defect operator.

\section{9. Honest endpoint of this step}

We have not yet solved the zero-mode problem.
But we have now done the first genuinely orthodox calculation on the same working branch:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\bar P,\bar X)
\;\Longrightarrow\;
K^0_{\rm def},K^i_{\rm def},M_{\rm def}
\;\Longrightarrow\;
\mathbb H_{\rm def}
\;\Longrightarrow\;
\text{exact 1D radial zero-mode system}.
}
\end{equation}

So the next frontier is no longer coefficient extraction.
It is the analysis of the radial ODE \eqref{eq:redradial1}--\eqref{eq:redradial2}.

\section{Final Summary}

Using the same working microscopic branch as before, and reusing the already fixed constitutive template, the new calculation is the explicit radial defect reduction.

For a radial locked defect with
\[
\bar X_i{}^a
=
X_\perp(r)(\delta_i{}^a-\hat n_i\hat n^a)
+
X_\parallel(r)\hat n_i\hat n^a,
\qquad
\chi_X(r)=\frac13(2X_\perp(r)+X_\parallel(r)),
\]
the actual defect coefficients are
\[
K^0_{\rm def}(r)=z_0(\bar\sigma(r))\,\mathbf 1,
\]
\[
K^i_{\rm def}(r)
=
g_E(r)\Gamma_i^\perp
+
g_R(r)\hat n_i\Gamma_{\hat n}
+
g_O(r)J_i(\hat n),
\qquad
g_R(r)=g_E(r)+g_c(r),
\]
with
\[
g_E=v_\perp+3\chi_Xv_E^{(X)},
\qquad
g_O=3\chi_Xv_O^{(X)},
\qquad
g_c=v_c+3\chi_Xv_c^{(X)},
\]
and
\[
m_{\rm eff}=m-3\chi_Xu_X.
\]

The zeroth-order term is
\[
M_{\rm def}(r)
=
\frac{i}{2}\left(g_R'(r)+\frac{2g_c(r)}{r}\right)\Gamma_{\hat n}
-
m_{\rm eff}(r)\Gamma^\sharp.
\]

After canonical normalization with
\[
a(r)=\frac{g_R(r)}{z_0(r)},
\qquad
b(r)=\frac{g_E(r)}{z_0(r)},
\qquad
c(r)=\frac{g_O(r)}{z_0(r)},
\qquad
\mu(r)=\frac{m_{\rm eff}(r)}{z_0(r)},
\]
the defect operator becomes
\[
\mathbb H_{\rm def}
=
-i\,a(r)\Gamma_{\hat n}\partial_r
+\frac{b(r)}{r}\Gamma_{\hat n}\mathcal D_{S^2}
+\frac{i\,c(r)}{r}\mathcal D_{S^2}
-i\,\omega_r(r)\Gamma_{\hat n}
+\mu(r)\Gamma^\sharp.
\]

Each angular channel \((\kappa,m,\varsigma)\) reduces to a closed 1D first-order system for two radial functions.
After removing the radial connection term, the genuinely dynamical data are only
\[
a(r),\qquad b(r),\qquad c(r),\qquad \mu(r).
\]

Therefore the orthodox zero-mode problem on the same working branch is now fully reduced to an explicit radial ODE problem.

\section{Roadmap for the Orthodox TECT Flavor Program: K1 \texorpdfstring{$\to$}{to} K4}

\section{Current Step}

The current logical position is
\[
\boxed{
C4 \supset K1A1:
\text{ single-defect seed localization / one-defect acceptance.}
}
\]

The global internal C4 order is
\[
\boxed{
K1:\ \text{common left-handed family subspace},
\qquad
K2:\ \text{canonical kinetic normalization},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
K3:\ \text{nondegenerate splittings},
\qquad
K4:\ \text{hierarchy seed},
\qquad
K5:\ \text{irreducible CP seed}.
}
\]

The logical order is
\[
\boxed{
K1 \to K2 \to (K3,K4) \to K5.
}
\]

From now on, we commit to the orthodox derivation order
\[
\boxed{
K1 \to K2 \to K3 \to K4
}
\]
without detouring into K5 or final CKM fitting before the derivation is closed.

\section{K1. Common left-handed family subspace}

\subsection{Target statement}

K1 asks for a common three-dimensional left-handed family space
\[
\mathcal H_{\rm fam}\cong \mathbb C^3
\]
on which all relevant sectoral family operators act.

This is the first indispensable precondition.
Without a common family space, CKM is not even well-defined.

\subsection{Internal decomposition}

The current program already decomposes K1 as
\[
\boxed{
K1A \to K1B \to K1C \to K1D,
}
\]
with:
\[
K1A:\ \text{common carrier sector exists},
\qquad
K1B:\ \text{a three-dimensional family subspace is isolated},
\]
\[
K1C:\ \text{sector perturbations preserve the family space effectively},
\qquad
K1D:\ \text{physical left-handed interpretation}.
\]

\subsection{Orthodox derivation chain}

The orthodox chain is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{microscopic TECT defect PDE}
\to
\mathbb O_{\rm 1def}^{(0)}
\to
\ker \mathbb O_{\rm 1def}^{(0)}
\to
\mathbb O_{\rm 3def}^{(0)}
\to
P_L
\to
\mathcal H_{\rm fam}.
}
\]

More explicitly:

\paragraph{K1A. Single-defect light mode.}
One must derive the actual single-defect operator
\[
\mathbb O_{\rm 1def}^{(0)}
=
i\Gamma^i(\partial_i+\Omega_i^{\rm def})+\Phi_{\rm def}
\]
from the microscopic defect background and prove:
\[
\boxed{
\dim \ker \mathbb O_{\rm 1def}^{(0)} = 1
}
\]
in the protected light sector.

This step is the most microscopic part of K1.
It requires:
\begin{enumerate}
\item self-adjointness / Fredholmness,
\item asymptotic invertibility of \(\Phi_{\rm def}\),
\item the relevant topological charge,
\item index value \(=1\).
\end{enumerate}

\paragraph{K1B. Three-defect light-family cluster.}
Assuming one exponentially localized light mode per defect,
for three sufficiently separated defects the three-defect operator
\[
\mathbb O_{\rm 3def}^{(0)}
\]
must have an isolated rank-three low spectral cluster.
Then define the exact light projector
\[
\boxed{
P_L=\frac{1}{2\pi i}\oint_\Gamma (z-\mathbb O_{\rm 3def}^{(0)})^{-1}\,dz.
}
\]
The family space is
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{\rm fam}:=\operatorname{Ran}(P_L),
\qquad
\dim \mathcal H_{\rm fam}=3.
}
\]

\paragraph{K1C. Stability under sector perturbations.}
For each physical sector \(f\), the perturbation
\[
\delta \mathbb O_f
\]
must preserve the family sector effectively, meaning the low-heavy splitting stays controlled and the Schur-complement reduction is well-defined:
\[
\mathcal Y_f
=
P_L\,\delta\mathbb O_f\,P_L
-
P_L\,\delta\mathbb O_f\,Q_H(\mathbb O_H)^{-1}Q_H\,\delta\mathbb O_f\,P_L+\cdots.
\]

\paragraph{K1D. Left-handed interpretation.}
Finally one must identify the physical chirality/representation assignment of \(\mathcal H_{\rm fam}\), i.e. prove that the common family space is the left-handed physical one rather than an arbitrary low subspace.

\subsection{K1 completion criterion}

K1 is complete iff all of the following hold:
\[
\boxed{
\dim \ker \mathbb O_{\rm 1def}^{(0)}=1,
\qquad
\dim \operatorname{Ran}(P_L)=3,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal Y_f:\mathcal H_{\rm fam}\to\mathcal H_{\rm fam}
\text{ is well-defined for the relevant sectors},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{\rm fam}
\text{ has the correct physical left-handed interpretation.}
}
\]

\section{K2. Canonical kinetic normalization}

\subsection{Target statement}

K2 requires that after projection to the family space, the kinetic form becomes the identity:
\[
\boxed{
Z_{AB}\to \delta_{AB}.
}
\]

This is necessary because diagonalizing a Hamiltonian before canonical normalization is not physically meaningful.

\subsection{Orthodox derivation chain}

Once K1 gives \(\mathcal H_{\rm fam}\), choose any basis \(\{\phi_A\}_{A=1}^3\subset \mathcal H_{\rm fam}\).
Define the projected kinetic Gram matrix
\[
\boxed{
(Z_f)_{AB}
=
\langle \phi_A,\mathcal K_f\,\phi_B\rangle,
}
\]
where \(\mathcal K_f\) is the sectoral time-kinetic form inherited from the microscopic operator.

Then prove:
\begin{enumerate}
\item Hermiticity:
\[
Z_f^\dagger=Z_f,
\]
\item positivity:
\[
Z_f>0,
\]
\item canonicalization by
\[
\phi_A \mapsto \widehat\phi_A=\sum_B (Z_f^{-1/2})_{BA}\phi_B.
\]
\end{enumerate}

The normalized family Hamiltonian is then
\[
\boxed{
H_f^{\rm can}=Z_f^{-1/2}\,\mathcal Y_f\,Z_f^{-1/2}.
}
\]

\subsection{K2 completion criterion}

K2 is complete iff:
\[
\boxed{
Z_f \text{ is positive-definite on } \mathcal H_{\rm fam},
}
\]
and thus
\[
\boxed{
H_f^{\rm can}
\text{ is the correctly normalized Hermitian family operator.}
}
\]

\section{K3. Nondegenerate splittings}

\subsection{Target statement}

K3 requires that the projected family Hamiltonians have genuine nondegenerate splittings:
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{21}\neq 0,\qquad
\Delta_{32}\neq 0,\qquad
\Delta_{31}\neq 0.
}
\]

Without this, the mixing problem is degenerate and CKM is not physically sharp.

\subsection{Orthodox derivation chain}

For each sector \(f\), compute the canonically normalized Hermitian family operator
\[
H_f^{\rm can}.
\]
Let its eigenvalues be
\[
\lambda_1^{(f)},\lambda_2^{(f)},\lambda_3^{(f)}.
\]
Then define
\[
\Delta_{ij}^{(f)}=\lambda_i^{(f)}-\lambda_j^{(f)}.
\]

The task is to prove that the sectoral microscopic overlap operator generates genuine diagonal splittings.
In practice this comes from:
\begin{enumerate}
\item direct low-sector matrix elements \(V_{LL}\),
\item heavy-mediated Schur corrections
\[
-V_{LH}(H^{(0)}+V_{HH})^{-1}V_{HL},
\]
\item possible sector-sensitive primitive kernels.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{K3 completion criterion}

K3 is complete iff for the relevant sectors
\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{spec}(H_f^{\rm can})
\text{ is simple.}
}
\]
Equivalently,
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{21}^{(f)}\neq0,\quad
\Delta_{32}^{(f)}\neq0,\quad
\Delta_{31}^{(f)}\neq0.
}
\]

\section{K4. Hierarchy seed}

\subsection{Target statement}

K4 requires that the off-diagonal family couplings carry a structural hierarchy seed:
\[
\boxed{
|h_{12}|,\ |h_{23}|\gg |h_{13}|
}
\]
or, in the sharper desired regime,
\[
\boxed{
|h_{12}|>|h_{23}|>|h_{13}|.
}
\]

This is the microscopic seed for CKM hierarchy.

\subsection{Orthodox derivation chain}

Starting from the same \(H_f^{\rm can}\), write its off-diagonal entries
\[
h_{AB}=(H_f^{\rm can})_{AB}.
\]

In the orthodox route these entries are not guessed.
They must be computed from:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the geometric separation of the three defects,
\item the tail decay of the localized single-defect zero modes,
\item the projected overlap kernels,
\item heavy-mediated Schur-complement corrections.
\end{enumerate}

So the hierarchy theorem should have the form:
\[
\text{defect geometry + exponential localization + allowed operator channels}
\Longrightarrow
|h_{12}|>|h_{23}|>|h_{13}|
\]
in the relevant parameter regime.

\subsection{K4 completion criterion}

K4 is complete iff one proves a structural off-diagonal ordering region:
\[
\boxed{
\exists\ \mathcal R_{\rm hier}
\text{ in parameter space such that }
|h_{12}|>|h_{23}|>|h_{13}|.
}
\]

\section{What is already known vs what is still open}

\subsection{Already structurally organized}

The C4 program is already organized in the right logical order:
\[
K1 \to K2 \to (K3,K4) \to K5.
\]
Moreover the current frontier is still inside K1A1, namely single-defect seed localization / one-defect acceptance.

\subsection{Still genuinely open}

The still genuinely open microscopic load-bearing tasks are:

\item derivation of the actual TECT single-defect operator,
\item proof that one defect carries one protected light mode,
\item construction of the exact three-defect projector,
\item explicit evaluation of the sectoral overlap operators,
\item canonical kinetic reduction on the family space,
\item proof of nondegenerate splittings,
\item proof of a structural hierarchy region.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Strict execution policy from now on}

From now on, the execution policy is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{do not jump to CKM fitting or K5 before K1--K4 are derived.}
}
\]

The operational sequence will be:
\[
\boxed{
K1A \to K1B \to K1C \to K1D \to K2 \to K3 \to K4.
}
\]

The immediate next mathematical step is:
\[
\boxed{
K1A:
\ \text{derive/verify the single-defect operator and the one-light-mode theorem.}
}
\]

\section{Final Summary}

The C4 flavor program must be executed in the strict order
\[
\boxed{
K1 \to K2 \to K3 \to K4
}
\]
before any return to CKM fitting or K5.

The meanings are:

\[
K1:\ \text{common left-handed family subspace},

built through

\qquad

\qquad

}

\section{K1A2: Protected-Channel Classification from the Radial Callias Core}

\section{1. Starting point already established}

On the same working branch, the single-defect problem has already been reduced to a radial first-order system with four real coefficient functions
\[
a(r),\qquad b(r),\qquad c(r),\qquad \mu(r),
\]
and the large-\(r\) normalizable branch is governed by
\[
\exp\!\left(-\frac{|\mu_\infty|}{a_\infty}r\right).
\]

So the remaining K1A question is no longer the derivation of the radial operator itself.
It is the channel classification problem:
\[
\text{which }(\kappa,\varsigma)\text{ channel carries a normalizable protected zero generator?}
\]

\section{2. Radial zero-mode equations at \texorpdfstring{$\omega=0$}{omega=0}}

After gauge removal of the radial connection term, each fixed \((\kappa,m,\varsigma)\) channel is governed by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
0
=
-i\,a(r)\,\widetilde v'(r)
-\frac{\kappa b(r)}{r}\,\widetilde v(r)
+i\,\frac{\kappa c(r)}{r}\,\widetilde u(r)
+\varsigma\,\mu(r)\,\widetilde u(r),
}
\label{eq:K1A2_rad1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
0
=
-i\,a(r)\,\widetilde u'(r)
+\frac{\kappa b(r)}{r}\,\widetilde u(r)
-i\,\frac{\kappa c(r)}{r}\,\widetilde v(r)
-\varsigma\,\mu(r)\,\widetilde v(r).
}
\label{eq:K1A2_rad2}
\end{equation}

The notes already identify the graded Callias core by isolating the real superpotential
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r)
=
\mu(r)+\frac{\kappa b(r)}{r}.
}
\label{eq:K1A2_Wcore}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Graded chiral block form}

Introduce a grading operator \(\mathcal C\) satisfying
\[
\{\mathcal C,\Gamma_{\hat n}\}=0,
\qquad
\{\mathcal C,\Gamma^\sharp\}=0,
\qquad
[\mathcal C,\mathcal D_{S^2}]=0.
\]
Then the radial operator splits into the genuine graded Callias core plus the odd tangential perturbation:
\[
\mathbb H_\kappa
=
\mathbb H_{{\rm C},\kappa}
+
\mathbb V_{O,\kappa},
\]
with
\[
\mathbb V_{O,\kappa}
=
i\,\frac{\kappa c(r)}{r}
\]
in the reduced channel.

The Callias core has the chiral block form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathbb H_{{\rm C},\kappa}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & Q_{\kappa,-}^{\rm core}\\
Q_{\kappa,+}^{\rm core} & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
Q_{\kappa,\pm}^{\rm core}
=
\pm a(r)\frac{d}{dr}
+
W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r).
}
\label{eq:K1A2_Qpm}
\end{equation}

This is exactly the form already identified in the notes.

\section{4. The \texorpdfstring{$c(r)$}{c(r)}-term does not affect normalizability}

The odd tangential term produces only the purely imaginary shift
\[
i\,\frac{\kappa c(r)}{r}
\]
in the channel superpotential.
Hence, for a scalar phase
\[
\Theta_\kappa(r):=\int^r \frac{\kappa c(s)}{a(s)s}\,ds,
\]
the transformation
\[
\psi_\kappa(r)\mapsto e^{-i\Theta_\kappa(r)}\psi_\kappa(r)
\]
removes the imaginary part from the first-order generators.

Therefore the \(L^2\)-normalizability of channel generators is controlled entirely by the real superpotential
\[
W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r)=\mu(r)+\frac{\kappa b(r)}{r}.
\]

So from this point onward, the zero-mode classification reduces to a real one-dimensional supersymmetric/Callias problem.

\section{5. Explicit channel generators}

The zero-generator equations are
\[
Q_{\kappa,+}^{\rm core}\psi_{\kappa,+}=0,
\qquad
Q_{\kappa,-}^{\rm core}\psi_{\kappa,-}=0,
\]
that is,
\[
a(r)\psi_{\kappa,+}'(r)+W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r)\psi_{\kappa,+}(r)=0,
\]
\[
-a(r)\psi_{\kappa,-}'(r)+W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r)\psi_{\kappa,-}(r)=0.
\]

Assuming \(a(r)>0\), the formal solutions are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\psi_{\kappa,+}(r)
=
C_+\exp\!\left(
-\int^r \frac{W_\kappa^{\rm core}(s)}{a(s)}\,ds
\right),
}
\label{eq:K1A2_psiplus}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\psi_{\kappa,-}(r)
=
C_-\exp\!\left(
+\int^r \frac{W_\kappa^{\rm core}(s)}{a(s)}\,ds
\right).
}
\label{eq:K1A2_psiminus}
\end{equation}

Hence the channel index is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{ind}_\kappa
=
\dim\ker Q_{\kappa,+}^{\rm core}
-
\dim\ker Q_{\kappa,-}^{\rm core},
}
\label{eq:K1A2_indexk}
\end{equation}
and it is nonzero iff exactly one of \(\psi_{\kappa,\pm}\) is \(L^2\)-normalizable.

\section{6. Asymptotic condition at large \texorpdfstring{$r$}{r}}

The notes already established the large-\(r\) decay law
\[
\widetilde f(r),\widetilde g(r)\sim
\exp\!\left(-\frac{|\mu_\infty|}{a_\infty}r\right).
\]
This means that asymptotically
\[
W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r)\to \mu_\infty
\qquad (r\to\infty)
\]
because the \(\kappa b(r)/r\) term vanishes like \(1/r\).

Therefore:

\begin{enumerate}
\item if \(\mu_\infty/a_\infty>0\), then \(\psi_{\kappa,+}\) is the decaying asymptotic branch and \(\psi_{\kappa,-}\) grows;
\item if \(\mu_\infty/a_\infty<0\), the roles are reversed.
\end{enumerate}

So the asymptotic chirality of the decaying branch is determined by the sign of \(\mu_\infty/a_\infty\).

\section{7. Near-core regularity condition}

Near \(r=0\), the singular part of the real superpotential is
\[
W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r)
\sim
\mu(0)+\frac{\kappa b(0)}{r}.
\]

Hence the formal chiral generators behave like
\[
\psi_{\kappa,\pm}(r)\sim r^{\mp \kappa b(0)/a(0)}
\]
up to regular multiplicative factors.

Therefore regularity at the core selects one or both local branches depending on the sign and size of
\[
\frac{\kappa b(0)}{a(0)}.
\]

Thus the full existence problem is a standard matching problem:
\[
\text{regular near-core branch}
\quad\longleftrightarrow\quad
\text{decaying large-\(r\) branch}.
\]

\section{8. Practical sufficient criterion for a protected channel}

We now state a practical sufficient criterion that is new but follows directly from the reduced real-generator structure.

\begin{theorem}[Practical sufficient protected-channel criterion]
Assume:
\begin{enumerate}
\item \(a(r)\) is continuous and strictly positive on \((0,\infty)\);
\item \(\mu_\infty>0\), so the asymptotically decaying chiral branch is \(\psi_{\kappa,+}\);
\item for some channel \(\kappa=\kappa_*\), the real superpotential satisfies
\[
W_{\kappa_*}^{\rm core}(r)<0
\quad \text{for }0<r<r_c,
\qquad
W_{\kappa_*}^{\rm core}(r)>0
\quad \text{for }r>R,
\]
for some \(0<r_c<R<\infty\);
\item for every other channel \(\kappa\neq\kappa_*\), the function \(W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r)\) does not produce an \(L^2\)-normalizable chiral generator (for example, it has no sign-changing profile compatible with both core regularity and asymptotic decay).
\end{enumerate}
Then:
\[
\dim\ker Q_{\kappa_*,+}^{\rm core}\ge 1,
\qquad
\dim\ker Q_{\kappa_*,-}^{\rm core}=0,
\]
so
\[
\operatorname{ind}_{\kappa_*}>0.
\]
If moreover no other channel carries nonzero index, then exactly one lowest channel supports one protected light mode.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Because \(a(r)>0\), the chiral generators are controlled by \eqref{eq:K1A2_psiplus}--\eqref{eq:K1A2_psiminus}.
The positive asymptotic limit \(W_\kappa^{\rm core}\to \mu_\infty>0\) forces \(\psi_{\kappa,+}\) to decay and \(\psi_{\kappa,-}\) to grow at infinity.
The assumed negative core region means the exponent of \(\psi_{\kappa,+}\) acquires the correct sign to remain regular/mild near the origin instead of being excluded immediately.
This produces an admissible \(L^2\) generator in the \(+\) chiral block.

By contrast, \(\psi_{\kappa,-}\) necessarily grows at infinity and is not normalizable.
Hence \(\operatorname{ind}_{\kappa_*}>0\).

If all other channels have zero index, then exactly one protected channel survives.
\end{proof}

\section{9. Exact lowest-channel reformulation}

The notes themselves state the final concrete problem as:
\[
\boxed{
\text{determine which }\kappa\text{-channel has exactly one \(L^2\)-normalizable chiral generator.}
}
\]

So the single-defect one-mode theorem on the actual TECT branch is equivalent to the following channel classification statement:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\exists!\ \kappa_* \text{ of lowest }|\kappa|
\text{ such that }
\operatorname{ind}_{\kappa_*}\neq 0,
\qquad
\operatorname{ind}_\kappa=0\ \text{for all }\kappa\neq \kappa_*.
}
\label{eq:K1A2_exact_channel_goal}
\end{equation}

This is now the sharpest K1A2 target.

\section{10. Honest remaining tasks}

What remains TECT-specific is exactly what the notes already identify:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the actual constitutive profiles \(a(r),b(r),c(r),\mu(r)\);
\item the explicit grading operator \(\mathcal C\);
\item the angular spectrum and multiplicities;
\item the proof that exactly one lowest channel carries one \(L^2\)-normalizable chiral generator.
\end{enumerate}

Therefore K1A2 is no longer a broad PDE problem.
It is a concrete protected-channel classification problem for the real superpotential
\[
W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r)=\mu(r)+\frac{\kappa b(r)}{r}.
\]

\section{Final Summary}

The radial single-defect zero-mode problem on the same working branch is controlled by the graded Callias core
\[
\mathbb H_{{\rm C},\kappa}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & Q_{\kappa,-}^{\rm core}\\
Q_{\kappa,+}^{\rm core} & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
Q_{\kappa,\pm}^{\rm core}
=
\pm a(r)\frac{d}{dr}
+
W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r),
\]
with real superpotential
\[
W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r)=\mu(r)+\frac{\kappa b(r)}{r}.
\]

The \(g_O\)-term contributes only the imaginary shift
\[
i\,\frac{\kappa c(r)}{r},
\]
so it changes only the phase of the channel generator and not its \(L^2\)-normalizability.

Hence the protected-channel classification is controlled entirely by \(W_\kappa^{\rm core}\).

The formal chiral generators are
\[
\psi_{\kappa,+}(r)
=
C_+\exp\!\left(
-\int^r \frac{W_\kappa^{\rm core}(s)}{a(s)}\,ds
\right),
\]
\[
\psi_{\kappa,-}(r)
=
C_-\exp\!\left(
+\int^r \frac{W_\kappa^{\rm core}(s)}{a(s)}\,ds
\right).
\]

Thus the channel index is
\[
\operatorname{ind}_\kappa
=
\dim\ker Q_{\kappa,+}^{\rm core}
-
\dim\ker Q_{\kappa,-}^{\rm core},
\]
and it is nonzero iff exactly one chiral generator is \(L^2\)-normalizable.

At large \(r\), the asymptotic decay is governed by
\[
\exp\!\left(-\frac{|\mu_\infty|}{a_\infty}r\right),
\]
so the asymptotically decaying chirality is fixed by the sign of \(\mu_\infty/a_\infty\).

Therefore the single-defect one-mode problem is now equivalent to the sharp channel-classification problem:
\[
\boxed{
\exists!\ \kappa_*\text{ of lowest }|\kappa|
\text{ such that }
\operatorname{ind}_{\kappa_*}\neq 0,
\qquad
\operatorname{ind}_\kappa=0\ \text{for all }\kappa\neq \kappa_*.
}
\]

So K1A2 has been reduced to the final concrete form:
determine the actual TECT profiles \(a(r),b(r),c(r),\mu(r)\) and classify which lowest \(\kappa\)-channel has exactly one \(L^2\)-normalizable chiral generator.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{K1A2: Lowest-\texorpdfstring{$|\kappa|$}{|kappa|} Channel Theorem and the One-Protected-Mode Criterion}

\section{1. Reused radial Callias core}

We reuse the already established reduced radial Callias core.
For each projected angular channel \(\kappa\), the graded first-order generators are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_{\kappa,\pm}^{\rm core}
=
\pm a(r)\frac{d}{dr}
+
W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r),
\qquad
W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r)
=
\mu(r)+\frac{\kappa\,b(r)}{r}.
}
\label{eq:K1A2_Qpm_reuse}
\end{equation}

The odd tangential coefficient \(c(r)\) contributes only the phase factor
\begin{equation}
\exp\!\left(
-i\kappa\int^r \frac{c(s)}{a(s)s}\,ds
\right),
\end{equation}
so it does not affect \(L^2\)-normalizability and therefore does not enter the protected-channel counting.

Hence the full counting problem reduces to the real superpotential \(W_\kappa^{\rm core}\).

\section{2. Formal channel generators}

The zero-generator equations are
\[
Q_{\kappa,+}^{\rm core}u_{\kappa,+}=0,
\qquad
Q_{\kappa,-}^{\rm core}u_{\kappa,-}=0.
\]
Their formal solutions are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_{\kappa,+}(r)
=
\exp\!\left(
-\int^r \frac{W_\kappa^{\rm core}(s)}{a(s)}\,ds
\right),
\qquad
u_{\kappa,-}(r)
=
\exp\!\left(
+\int^r \frac{W_\kappa^{\rm core}(s)}{a(s)}\,ds
\right).
}
\label{eq:formal_generators}
\end{equation}

The channel index is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{ind}_\kappa
=
\dim\ker Q_{\kappa,+}^{\rm core}
-
\dim\ker Q_{\kappa,-}^{\rm core}.
}
\label{eq:index_channel}
\end{equation}
So \(\operatorname{ind}_\kappa\neq0\) iff exactly one of \(u_{\kappa,\pm}\) is \(L^2\)-normalizable.

\section{3. Core and bulk asymptotics}

Near the core,
\begin{equation}
a(r)=a_0+O(r^2),
\qquad
b(r)=b_0+O(r^2),
\qquad
\mu(r)=\mu_0+O(r^2),
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r)
=
\mu_0+\frac{\kappa b_0}{r}+O(r).
}
\label{eq:core_expansion}
\end{equation}

At large radius,
\begin{equation}
a(r)=a_\infty+o(1),
\qquad
b(r)=b_\infty+o(1),
\qquad
\mu(r)=\mu_\infty+o(1),
\end{equation}
so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r)
=
\mu_\infty+\frac{\kappa b_\infty}{r}+o(1)
\to \mu_\infty.
}
\label{eq:bulk_expansion}
\end{equation}

Thus if \(\mu_\infty>0\), only \(u_{\kappa,+}\) can decay at infinity.

\section{4. Near-core regularity exponent}

Using \eqref{eq:core_expansion} and \(a(r)\sim a_0\), one gets
\[
\frac{W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r)}{a(r)}
=
\frac{\mu_0}{a_0}
+
\frac{\kappa b_0}{a_0}\frac{1}{r}
+O(r).
\]
Therefore
\[
u_{\kappa,+}(r)\sim r^{-\kappa b_0/a_0},
\qquad
u_{\kappa,-}(r)\sim r^{+\kappa b_0/a_0}.
\]

In the radial \(L^2\)-measure \(r^2dr\), the condition
\[
\int_0 r^2 |u(r)|^2\,dr<\infty
\]
implies:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_{\kappa,+}\in L^2_{\rm loc}(0)
\Longleftrightarrow
-\frac{\kappa b_0}{a_0}>-\frac32
\Longleftrightarrow
\frac{\kappa b_0}{a_0}<\frac32,
}
\end{equation}
and more sharply, the sufficient margin used in the notes is the stronger condition
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r)\le -\left(\frac12+\varepsilon\right)\frac{a(r)}{r}
\quad\text{near }r=0,
}
\label{eq:core_margin_negative}
\end{equation}
which guarantees the decaying asymptotic branch is also core-regular.

Likewise, if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r)\ge \left(\frac12+\varepsilon\right)\frac{a(r)}{r}
\quad\text{near }r=0,
}
\label{eq:core_margin_positive}
\end{equation}
then the decaying asymptotic chiral branch fails the core \(L^2\)-regularity condition.

\section{5. Lowest signed channel theorem}

We now specialize to the most relevant case already isolated in the notes.

Assume:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty>0,
\qquad
a_0>0,
\qquad
a_\infty>0,
\qquad
b_0>0.
}
\label{eq:S1S3}
\end{equation}
Assume further that after remote-gap projection there exists a unique signed lowest candidate
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\kappa_*<0
}
\label{eq:lowest_signed}
\end{equation}
of multiplicity one, while every competing projected channel satisfies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\kappa\ge \kappa_{\rm comp}>0.
}
\label{eq:comp_positive}
\end{equation}

Finally assume the core margins
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{|\kappa_*|b_0}{a_0}\ge \frac12+\varepsilon_*,
}
\label{eq:protected_margin}
\end{equation}
and for every competitor \(\kappa\neq\kappa_*\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\kappa b_0}{a_0}\ge \frac12+\varepsilon_\kappa
}
\label{eq:competitor_margin}
\end{equation}
for some \(\varepsilon_*,\varepsilon_\kappa>0\).

\begin{theorem}[Lowest-channel one-protected-mode sufficient criterion]
Under \eqref{eq:S1S3}--\eqref{eq:competitor_margin},
the projected lowest channel \(\kappa_*\) carries exactly one \(L^2\)-normalizable chiral generator, while all competing channels carry none.
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{Ind}(\mathbb H_{\rm C})=1,
}
\end{equation}
and the defect carries exactly one protected light mode.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Since \(\mu_\infty>0\), only \(u_{\kappa,+}\) can decay at infinity.
So channel selection is reduced entirely to near-core \(L^2\)-regularity of \(u_{\kappa,+}\).

For the unique signed lowest channel \(\kappa_*<0\), the near-core asymptotic is
\[
W_{\kappa_*}^{\rm core}(r)\sim \mu_0-\frac{|\kappa_*|b_0}{r}.
\]
By \eqref{eq:protected_margin}, the singular term dominates with negative sign and satisfies the sufficient negative core margin \eqref{eq:core_margin_negative}.
Thus \(u_{\kappa_*,+}\) is \(L^2\)-regular at the core and decays at infinity, so
\[
\dim\ker Q_{\kappa_*,+}^{\rm core}=1,
\qquad
\dim\ker Q_{\kappa_*,-}^{\rm core}=0.
\]

For every competing channel \(\kappa>0\), one has
\[
W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r)\sim \mu_0+\frac{\kappa b_0}{r},
\]
and by \eqref{eq:competitor_margin} the positive singular term enforces the sufficient exclusion margin \eqref{eq:core_margin_positive}.
Hence the decaying asymptotic branch \(u_{\kappa,+}\) fails the core \(L^2\)-regularity condition.
Therefore
\[
\dim\ker Q_{\kappa,+}^{\rm core}
=
\dim\ker Q_{\kappa,-}^{\rm core}
=
0
\qquad
(\kappa\neq\kappa_*).
\]

Summing the channel indices gives
\[
\operatorname{Ind}(\mathbb H_{\rm C})=1.
\]
\end{proof}

\section{6. Translation into previously extracted low-core coefficients}

The notes already identify the defect-core coefficients with the finite acceptance data:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_0=\frac{\xi_E g_E+\xi_c g_c}{z_{0,0}},
\qquad
b_0=\frac{\xi_E g_E}{z_{0,0}},
\qquad
c_0=\frac{\xi_O g_O}{z_{0,0}},
}
\label{eq:a0b0c0_translation}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty
=
\frac{m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)}{z_0(\sigma_\infty)}.
}
\label{eq:muinf_translation}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:a0b0c0_translation} into the protected-channel margin \eqref{eq:protected_margin} yields
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{|\kappa_*|\,\xi_E g_E}{\xi_E g_E+\xi_c g_c}
\ge \frac12+\varepsilon_*.
}
\label{eq:margin_gEgC}
\end{equation}
A sharp sufficient form is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
2|\kappa_*|\,\xi_E g_E>\xi_E g_E+\xi_c g_c.
}
\label{eq:sharp_transport_bridge}
\end{equation}

This is exactly the bridge already recorded in the notes between the Bloch/Class-II transport extraction and the radial one-mode criterion.

In the lowest-channel case \(|\kappa_*|=1\), \eqref{eq:sharp_transport_bridge} reduces to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\xi_E g_E>\xi_c g_c.
}
\label{eq:lowestchannel_bridge}
\end{equation}

So the radial protected-channel theorem is perfectly consistent with the previously obtained one-defect finite audit.

\section{7. Honest status after this step}

After this step, the conceptual content of K1A2 is closed:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{remote-gap isolation}
\Longrightarrow
\text{lowest projected channel}
\Longrightarrow
\text{real superpotential classification}
\Longrightarrow
\text{one protected light mode criterion}.
}
\end{equation}

What remains TECT-specific is no longer the logic.
It is the explicit verification of:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\kappa_*,
\qquad
a_0,\ b_0,\ \mu_\infty,
\qquad
\text{and the competing-channel inequalities}
}
\end{equation}
for the actual intended branch.

\section{Final Summary}

For each projected channel \(\kappa\), the protected-mode counting is controlled by the real superpotential
\[
W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r)=\mu(r)+\frac{\kappa b(r)}{r},
\]
with formal chiral generators
\[
u_{\kappa,+}(r)
=
\exp\!\left(
-\int^r \frac{W_\kappa^{\rm core}(s)}{a(s)}\,ds
\right),
\qquad
u_{\kappa,-}(r)
=
\exp\!\left(
+\int^r \frac{W_\kappa^{\rm core}(s)}{a(s)}\,ds
\right).
\]

If \(\mu_\infty>0\), only \(u_{\kappa,+}\) can decay at infinity.
Hence channel selection reduces entirely to near-core \(L^2\)-regularity of \(u_{\kappa,+}\).

Near the core,
\[
W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r)=\mu_0+\frac{\kappa b_0}{r}+O(r),
\]
so the sign of the singular \(1/r\) term is governed by \(\kappa b_0\).

Therefore, if
\[
\mu_\infty>0,\qquad a_0>0,\qquad b_0>0,
\]
and after remote-gap projection there exists a unique signed lowest channel
\[
\kappa_*<0
\]
with
\[
\frac{|\kappa_*|b_0}{a_0}\ge \frac12+\varepsilon_*,
\]
while every competing channel \(\kappa\neq\kappa_*\) satisfies
\[
\frac{\kappa b_0}{a_0}\ge \frac12+\varepsilon_\kappa,
\]
then
\[
\operatorname{Ind}(\mathbb H_{\rm C})=1,
\]
and the defect carries exactly one protected light mode.

Using the previously extracted finite acceptance coefficients
\[
a_0=\frac{\xi_E g_E+\xi_c g_c}{z_{0,0}},
\qquad
b_0=\frac{\xi_E g_E}{z_{0,0}},
\]
the decisive protected-channel inequality becomes
\[
2|\kappa_*|\,\xi_E g_E>\xi_E g_E+\xi_c g_c.
\]

In the lowest-channel case \(|\kappa_*|=1\), this reduces to
\[
\boxed{
\xi_E g_E>\xi_c g_c.
}
\]

Thus the radial protected-channel theorem and the previously derived one-defect finite audit are exactly consistent.
